# SBTi Services — Criteria Assessment Indicators V1.6
**Source:** SBTi Services Criteria Assessment Indicators, Version 1.6, March 2026
**Effective date:** March 19, 2026
**Pages:** 404
**Publisher:** SBTi Services Limited (wholly owned subsidiary of Science Based Targets initiative)
**Registered address:** 66 Lincoln's Inn Fields, London, England, WC2A 3LH (registered in England and Wales, number 15181058)
**Contact:** sbtiservices.com | info@sbtiservices.com

---

## ABOUT SBTi SERVICES

SBTi Services Limited is a wholly owned subsidiary of the Science Based Targets initiative, a corporate climate action organization and standard-setter that enables companies and financial institutions worldwide to play their part in combating the climate crisis. SBTi Services is a distinct legal entity and operates independently from the standard-setter, the Science Based Targets initiative.

SBTi Services checks and validates climate targets, validating the decarbonization goals of corporations, financial institutions and SMEs worldwide. By validating their climate targets, businesses demonstrate an understanding of their minimum decarbonization requirements by which customers and investors can measure them.

To be validated, companies must create greenhouse gas inventories and apply the Science Based Targets initiative's thorough methodologies for calculating decarbonization targets and submit these to SBTi Services for validation. Validators at SBTi Services check companies' and financial institutions' climate targets with standards developed by the Science Based Targets initiative.

SBTi Services is a trading subsidiary company, with any profits generated from commercial activities used to support its parent the Science Based Targets initiative, a charity registered in England and Wales.

---

## DISCLAIMER

The checklist of Criteria Assessment Indicators provided by SBTi Services Limited ("SBTi Services") are intended to serve as a general guide for organizations seeking validation against the SBTi Corporate Near-Term Criteria and SBTi Corporate Net-Zero Standard and sector guidance. This checklist outlines key indicators used during the SBTi Services' target validation process and are based on the most current version of the standard at the time of publication. However, they are not exhaustive, and additional requirements may apply depending on the specific circumstances of each validation.

The use of this checklist does not guarantee compliance with the standard, nor does it constitute a formal approval of SBTi targets. The actual SBTi target validation process conducted by SBTi Services involves a comprehensive review of all relevant factors, and final decisions are based on a detailed assessment by our qualified team.

SBTi Services disclaims all liability for errors or omissions in this checklist or for actions taken in reliance on their content. The checklist may be updated or modified at any time by SBTi Services to reflect changes in standards, guidance or applicable regulations as developed or applied by the Science Based Targets initiative ("SBTi") or SBTi Services. Users are encouraged to consult the most recent version and to seek professional advice if necessary.

## INTRODUCTION

SBTi Services independently assesses corporate and financial institutions' science-based emission reduction targets against SBTi Standards. To support this service, the Criteria Assessment Tables in this document outline the major checks conducted by SBTi Services during the validation process, to ensure conformance with SBTi Criteria.

The Criteria Assessment Indicators (CAI) described in this document are provided as control points which will be used to evaluate submitted information during the target validation process. Conformity with the CAI gives confidence that the company is in compliance with the SBTi Standard(s) under which they are submitting targets. The CAI found in the following sections of this document represent a clarification and formalization of the existing process followed by the Target Validation Team to assess alignment of all corporate and financial institution submissions with SBTi Criteria, SBTi Sector Guidance and GHG Protocol Corporate Standard, Scope 2 Guidance, and Corporate Value Chain Standard. The publication of the CAI seeks to provide clarity for stakeholders and does not signify any additional requirements for companies setting science-based targets, beyond what has been required of all companies submitting under SBTi applicable Criteria.

Any updates made to the contents of this document will be communicated in SBTi Services website to all companies before these become applicable. SBTi Services urges companies to regularly review our website to ensure these updates are not missed.

This document uses precise language to indicate requirements, recommendations and permissible options that companies may choose to follow. In certain exceptional instances, sector-specific CAI may supersede requirements outlined in the sector-agnostic CAI.

- The terms **"shall"** or **"must"** are used throughout this document to indicate what is required for companies to be in conformance with SBTi Criteria.
- The term **"should"** is used to indicate a recommendation.
- The term **"may"** is used to indicate that an option is permissible or allowable.

This document is intended for corporates and financial institutions submitting targets to SBTi Services. Companies should utilize this document while completing the Corporate or Financial Institutions Submission Form in SBTi Services Validation Portal — henceforth referred to as "the submission form" — to ensure that any proposed targets meet all relevant criteria. The 'description' column provides a detailed explanation of the CAI, which can be understood as the various checks conducted to ensure conformity with the SBTi Criteria. The 'minimum documentation required' column outlines the information needed to assess conformity with each criteria assessment indicator, and stipulates where (if relevant) in the submission form to provide this information or if supplemental documentation is required.

The Target Validation Team will review all submissions to ensure that all CAI are met for any target submission to be approved. The Target Validation Team reserves the right to request additional information during the validation process, where further explanation or evidence is needed to clarify alignment with any criteria assessment indicators.

For SBTi Services to provide any of its services, corporates and financial institutions must provide information that is accurate and complete at the time of submission and must update such information in order that all submissions are and remain accurate and complete at all times. In the case SBTi Services determines that all or part of the information provided is inaccurate, incomplete or confirms that it has been intentionally hidden or forged, this could be a reason to suspend or void the validation process.

All data collected during the validation is handled as described in the SBTi Data Security and Confidentiality Policy and in conformance with the validation services agreement.

## CRITERIA ASSESSMENT INDICATORS

## ASSESSMENT OF SBTi CRITERIA FOR NEAR-TERM TARGETS

### Table 1. Near-Term Criteria Assessment Table

*[pages 9–70]*

**Table columns:** Criteria Assessment Indicator | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required

#### NT C1 — Organizational Boundary

**Criteria header:** NT C1 - Organizational boundary: Companies should submit targets only at the parent- or group level, not the subsidiary level. Parent companies shall include the emissions of all subsidiaries in their target submission, in accordance with the boundary criteria.* In cases where both parent companies and subsidiaries submit targets, the parent company's target must also include the emissions of the subsidiary if it falls within the parent company's emissions boundary given the chosen inventory consolidation approach.**,***

*\* As outlined in NT C2 to NT C6, and NZ C2 to NZ C7.*
*\*\* Brands, licensees, and/or specific regions or business divisions of a company will not be accepted as separate targets unless they fall outside of a parent company's chosen consolidation approach.*
*\*\*\* Companies must integrate emissions from their structural changes into their GHG inventory within a reasonable timeframe.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **1.1 Disclosure of organizational boundary** | GHG Accounting | Companies must disclose the organizational boundary approach chosen, and justify the appropriateness of the approach used. Any deviations from the consolidation approach must be indicated and highlighted in the supporting evidence. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; Questions: R331, R332, R333, S334; Selection of consolidation approach and explanation of choice (e.g., choice aligns with financial reporting and the company provides a link to the financial report). |
| **1.2 Disclosure of organizational structure** | GHG Accounting | Companies must submit a diagram or visual representation of the company structure to clearly demonstrate the entities that are within the organizational boundary. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; Questions: R335111; Upload of "company structure template.csv" file available in the Validation Portal with all the relevant details such as percentage ownership the reporting company has in all worldwide subsidiaries, joint ventures, and other entities disclosed. |
| **1.3 Inclusion of subsidiaries** | GHG Accounting | Companies must include all worldwide subsidiaries in accordance with the chosen consolidation approach (e.g., operational control) to determine the organizational boundary. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; Questions: R335111; Upload of "company structure template.csv" file available in the Validation Portal with all the relevant details such as percentage ownership the reporting company has in all worldwide subsidiaries, joint ventures, and other entities disclosed. Indication of whether the company has operational control over each subsidiary listed within the csv file. |
| **1.4 Integration of structural changes into GHG inventory** | GHG Accounting | Companies must integrate emissions from their structural changes into their GHG inventory within a reasonable timeframe as per the GHG Protocol Corporate Standard Chapter 5 for recalculating base year emissions (pages 35–39). Companies should make this integration within a year of the completion of a full reporting cycle after the structural change. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; GHG Inventory tab - Overview; Questions: S341, S3411, S342, S3421; Provision of details regarding all mergers, acquisitions, and divestments, along with a quantification of the emissions impact of the structural change. Indication of whether structural changes have been incorporated into the base year and most recent year inventory. If any have not, justification is needed. Justifications include but are not limited to: occurred in the last year and haven't been integrated yet, changes are cumulatively below the 5% recalculation threshold, or entities have been excluded as part of the 5% threshold. |
| **1.5 Disclosure of exclusions** | GHG Accounting | Companies must transparently disclose if any entities that are within the organizational boundary have been omitted from the reporting. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: R335111, S52, S522, S61 (including all sub-questions); Provision of details of excluded entities within the "Company structure template.csv" file, and quantification of any excluded emissions from these entities in tCO₂e. |
| **1.6 Disclosure of unconsolidated entities** | GHG Accounting | Companies using the financial or operational control approach must disclose in scope 3 category 15 those emissions coming from entities in which they have a stake but which are not within their organizational boundary. This does not apply to companies using the equity share consolidation approach, which must disclose emissions from all entities in which they have a stake within their organizational boundary proportional to the equity held in each entity, as per the GHG Protocol Corporate Standard. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Investments; Questions: R335111, S6151, S61513; Disclosure of unconsolidated entities and any entities outside a company's organizational boundary within the "Company structure template.csv", including quantification of associated emissions from these entities in tCO₂e. |
| **1.7 Alignment of organizational boundaries** | (no applicability specified) | Companies shall not set targets at the brand, licensee, and/or specific region or business division level. Companies must ensure all subsidiaries relevant to business activities and operations do legally fall under the entity that submitted to SBTi Services. | GHG Inventory tab - General questions; Questions: R335111; Upload of "company structure template.csv" file available in the Validation Portal with all the relevant details such as percentage ownership the reporting company has in all worldwide subsidiaries, joint ventures, and other entities disclosed. Indication of whether the company has operational control over each subsidiary listed within the csv file. |

#### NT C2 — Greenhouse Gases

**Criteria header:** NT C2 - Greenhouse gasses: The targets shall cover all relevant emissions of the seven GHGs as required by the GHG Protocol Corporate Standard.*

*\* The seven GHGs are carbon dioxide (CO₂), methane (CH₄), nitrous oxide (N₂O), hydrofluorocarbons (HFCs), perfluorocarbons (PFCs), sulfur hexafluoride (SF₆), and nitrogen trifluoride (NF₃).*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **2.1 Inclusion of greenhouse gasses** | GHG Accounting | As indicated in the GHG Protocol Corporate Standard (Required Greenhouse Gases in Inventories, Accounting and Reporting Standard Amendment (February, 2013) to include NF3), the GHG inventory must cover all relevant emissions of the seven different GHGs or classes of GHGs covered by the UNFCCC/Kyoto Protocol. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - General questions; Questions: S321; Confirmation. |
| **2.2 Disclosure of exclusions** | GHG Accounting | Companies must justify and include any exclusions in the submission form. Please note being unable to measure a gas is not a valid reason for exclusion. Exclusions must be calculated based on the entire gross inventory and insignificant categories still need to be accounted for in the inventory in tCO₂e. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: R335111, S52, S522, S61; Confirmation. Confirmation that any GHG exclusion along with other exclusions do not amount to over 5%. If a gas is deemed not relevant because it isn't used in the reporting company's operations, an explanation must be provided with further contextual information. |

---

#### NT C3 — Scope 1 and Scope 2

**Criteria header:** NT C3 - Scope 1 and scope 2: The targets shall cover company-wide scope 1 and scope 2 emissions, as defined by the GHG Protocol Corporate Standard.*

*\* GHG accounting that is not proven to adhere to the GHG Protocol accounting standard and the SBTi criteria assessment indicators will not be accepted by the SBTi.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **3.1 Inclusion of scope 1 activities** | GHG Accounting | Companies must include all direct GHG emissions occurring from sources that are owned or controlled by the reporting company based on the consolidation approach chosen*. Refer to GHG Protocol Corporate Standard Chapter 4 page 27 for examples of direct GHG emissions included in scope 1. *See SBTi Near-Term Criterion 5 for exclusionary allowances. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - Scope 1; Questions: S52; Description of key scope 1 business activities. |
| **3.2 Inclusion of scope 2 activities** | GHG Accounting | Companies must include all GHG emissions from the generation of purchased electricity, heat, steam and cooling based on the consolidation approach chosen.* *See SBTi Near-Term Criterion 5 for exclusionary allowances. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - Scope 2; Questions: S522; Description of key scope 2 business activities. |
| **3.3 SBTi scope 1 and 2 Criteria Assessment Indicators** | GHG Accounting | GHG accounting must be in accordance with SBTi GHG Accounting Criteria Assessment Indicators 1.1–2.3. | Demonstration of objective evidence needed for GHG Accounting Criteria Assessment Indicators 1.1–2.3. |

---

#### NT C4 — Scope 3

**Criteria header:** NT C4 - Scope 3: If a company's relevant scope 3 emissions are 40% or more of total scope 1, 2, and 3 emissions, they shall be included in near-term science-based targets. All companies involved in the sale or distribution of natural gas and/or other fossil fuels shall set separate scope 3 targets for the use of sold products, irrespective of the share of these emissions compared to the total scope 1, 2, and 3 emissions of the company.

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **4.1 Complete disclosure of GHG inventory based on GHG Protocol Scope 3 Standard** | GHG Accounting | Companies must disclose the entire GHG inventory in line with the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Scope 3 Standard. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - Scope 3; GHG Inventory - Overview; Questions: S61, S712; Provision of a GHG inventory for all activities in the reporting year, and demonstration of objective evidence needed for the GHG accounting Criteria Assessment Indicators. |
| **4.2 Scope 3 category 11 for companies involved in the distribution or sale of fossil fuel products** | Target Setting | Companies involved in the distribution or sale of fossil fuel products must set a standalone 1.5°C target over use of sold products covering all the scope 3 category 11 emissions corresponding to the combustion of the distributed and/or sold fossil fuels, regardless of the share of emissions their scope 3 inventory represents. | Portal Location: Registration - Eligibility; Targets tab - Add near-term target - Sold or distributed fossil fuels; Questions: S11114, S11119, R2562, R2651; Demonstration of objective evidence needed for SBTi Near-Term Criterion 22 and Criterion 23. |
| **4.3 Scope 3 target eligibility for near-term targets** | Target Setting | Companies with total scope 3 GHG emissions equal to or exceeding 40%* of total scope 1, 2 and 3 emissions must set scope 3 targets, considering the aggregated energy & industrial and FLAG-related emissions when separate inventories are reported. *If scope 3 emissions make up 39.9% or higher of total emissions, this will be rounded up to 40% and a scope 3 target is mandatory. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - Overview; Questions: S741; Confirmation and breakdown of key scope 3 GHG emissions to demonstrate that the total scope 3 emissions equal less than 40% of total emissions, plus confirmation that there is no involvement in the sale or distribution of fossil fuel products. |
| **4.4 Scope 3 target eligibility for near-term targets, most recent year** | Target Setting | Companies with total scope 3 GHG emissions equal to or exceeding 40% in the most recent year must set scope 3 targets considering the aggregated energy & industrial and FLAG-related emissions when separate inventories are reported. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - Scope 3; Questions: S61; Confirmation and breakdown of key scope 3 GHG emissions to demonstrate that the total scope 3 emissions equal less than 40% of total emissions in the most recent year. |

---

#### NT C5 — Scope 1, 2, and 3 Allowable Exclusions

**Criteria header:** NT C5 - Scope 1, 2, and 3 allowable exclusions: Companies shall not exclude more than 5% of total combined scope 1 and scope 2 emissions from either the boundary of the GHG inventory or the target boundary.*,** Companies shall not exclude more than 5% of emissions from their total scope 3 GHG inventory.*** Scope 3 target boundary requirements are outlined in C6.

*\* The total targeted scope 1 and 2 emissions shall be greater than or equal to 95% of total (reported + excluded) scope 1 and 2 emissions. This means that a company shall not exclude 5% from the inventory boundary and then also exclude a further 5% from the target boundary.*
*\*\* Where a company's scope 1 or 2 emissions are deemed immaterial (i.e., under 5% of total combined scope 1 and 2 emissions), companies may set their SBT solely on the scope (either scope 1 or scope 2) that covers more than 95% of the total scope 1 and 2 emissions. The company must continue to report on both scopes and adjust their targets as needed, in accordance with the GHG Protocol's principle of completeness, and as per C26 and C27.*
*\*\*\* The SBTi does not recognize emissions perceived to be "negligible" as a rationale for not reporting them. Even if emissions from certain activities or operations are perceived to be negligible, these emissions still must be quantified and reported in the reporting company's GHG inventory or disclosed as an exclusion.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **5.1 Scope 1 and 2 exclusion threshold** | GHG Accounting | Total exclusions from the reporting company's scope 1 and 2 inventory and target boundary combined must not exceed 5% of the total scope 1 and 2 emissions calculated.* *Where the reporting company's scope 1 or 2 emissions are less than 5% of total combined scope 1 and 2 emissions, companies may set their SBT solely on the scope (either scope 1 or scope 2) that covers more than 95% of the total scope 1 and 2 emissions. Companies must continue to report on both scopes and adjust their targets as needed, according to the GHG Protocol's principle of completeness, and as per C32 and C33. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - Scope 1; GHG Inventory - Scope 2; Questions: S52, S522; Provision of the scope 1 and 2 breakdown table with quantification and description of any exclusions from the scope 1 and 2 inventory. |
| **5.2 Scope 3 exclusion threshold** | GHG Accounting | Total exclusions from the reporting company's scope 3 inventory must not exceed 5% of the total scope 3 emissions calculated.* *The SBTi does not recognize emissions perceived to be "negligible" as a rationale for not reporting them. Even if emissions from certain activities or operations are perceived to be negligible, these emissions still must be quantified and reported in the reporting company's GHG inventory. This is regardless of whether the reporting [continued on next page] | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - Scope 3; Questions: S613 through S6153; Quantitatively list and describe any exclusions from the scope 3 inventory within relevant scope 3 category specific breakdown tables. |

---

*[pages 21–40 content below]*

| **5.3 Allowable exclusions based on immateriality** | GHG Accounting | Companies must account for all potential emissions sources and have calculated the total magnitude of emissions in tCO₂e before any emissions are excluded. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - Scope 1; GHG Inventory - Scope 2; GHG Inventory - Scope 3; Questions: S52, S522, S61; Provision of details on excluded emissions in scope 1 and 2, and scope 3 category specific breakdown tables including information on how these emissions were calculated. |
| **5.4 Monitoring of exclusion thresholds** | GHG Accounting | Exclusions must be monitored throughout the target timeframe. Any exclusions that breach the 5% threshold must be brought into the inventory boundary. | Portal Location: Progress and reporting; Questions: S1211, S1214; Confirmation that exclusions will be quantified and tracked on an annual basis along with all other GHG emissions. |

#### NT C6 — Scope 3 Emissions Coverage for Near-Term Targets

**Criteria header:** NT C6 - Scope 3 emissions coverage for near-term targets: Companies shall set one or more emission reduction near-term targets and/or supplier or customer engagement targets that collectively cover(s) at least 67% of total reported and excluded scope 3 emissions considering the minimum boundary of each category in conformance with the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain (Scope 3) Accounting and Reporting Standard.*

*\* GHG accounting that is not proven to adhere to the GHG Protocol minimum boundaries and the SBTi criteria assessment indicators will not be accepted by the SBTi.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **6.1 Assessment of scope 3 target boundary coverage** | Target Setting | Companies must set scope 3 targets that collectively cover at least 67% of total mandatory (reported and excluded) scope 3 emissions, not taking into account any optional emissions reported, as per the minimum boundary defined in the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain (Scope 3) Accounting and Reporting Standard and SBTi GHG Accounting Criteria Assessment Indicators. Companies must ensure this minimum coverage is met in the base year inventory. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term target; Demonstration of sufficient target coverage, showcasing which scope 3 categories are covered under each target set. Excluded emissions must be taken into account in the total scope 3 emissions when calculating the required coverage. Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. |
| **6.2 Disclosure of scope 3 beyond the minimum boundary emissions** | Target Setting | Optional emissions as per the GHG Protocol must be reported separately and must be covered under a different target. Optional targets (if applicable) must not be counted towards the 67% minimum coverage threshold, and excluded emissions must be taken into account when calculating the required coverage. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory - Scope 3; Targets tab - Add near-term beyond minimum boundary target; Questions: S6418, S5518, S6618, S6718, S6818, S6918, S61118, S61218, S61318, S61418, S61518; S11714, S11814; Demonstration, through separate scope 3 beyond minimum boundary reporting and target coverage tables, that optional targets (if applicable) have not been counted towards the 67% minimum coverage threshold. If a company wishes to cover optional emissions with a target, demonstration that a beyond minimum boundary target has been separately modeled and set. |

---

#### NT C7 — Method Validity

**Criteria header:** NT C7 - Method validity: Targets must be modeled using the latest version of methods and tools approved by the SBTi. Targets modeled using previous versions of the tools or methods may only be submitted to the SBTi for validation within 6 months of the publication of the revised method or sector-specific tools.

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **7.1 Target setting method applicability** | Target Setting | Companies must use an eligible target setting approach and version of the Corporate Near-term Tool to model each target. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add target; Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. For SDA targets where it is required to use and upload the SBTi sector specific target setting tools in the validation portal, companies must refer to the official near-term and long-term target setting tools published on the SBTi website. Any tool used must be uploaded in the format of an excel file. |
| **7.2 Target setting method validity** | Target Setting | Companies must check that the version of the tool used is valid before sending targets for SBTi validation. Companies have six months from the date a new tool is published to continue using the latest legacy version, unless otherwise noted. After that six month grace period, all companies must use the most up to date version available. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add target; Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. For SDA targets where it is required to use and upload the SBTi sector specific target setting tools in the validation portal, companies must refer to the official near-term and long-term target setting tools published on the SBTi website. Any tool used must be uploaded in the format of an excel file. |

---

#### NT C8 — Scope 2 Accounting Approach

**Criteria header:** NT C8 - Scope 2 accounting approach: Companies shall disclose whether they are using a location- or market-based accounting approach as per the GHG Protocol Scope 2 Guidance to calculate base year emissions and to track performance against a science-based target. The GHG Protocol requires measuring and reporting scope 2 emissions using both approaches. However, a single and consistent approach must be used for setting and tracking progress toward a SBT (e.g., using location-based approach for both target setting and progress tracking).

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **8.1 Scope 2 target setting** | Target Setting | Companies must use calculation methods consistent with the GHG Protocol Corporate Standard to report scope 2 emissions for both location-based and market-based scope 2 accounting, following the corresponding emission factor hierarchies in the GHG Protocol Scope 2 Guidance (tables 6.2 and 6.3 respectively). A single scope 2 accounting approach must be selected for the purpose of target setting. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; Questions: S521, S522; Selection of one scope 2 method and confirmation that the chosen method will be used consistently for tracking target progress. |
| **8.2 Scope 2 reduction strategy** | GHG Accounting | A scope 2 accounting approach and reduction strategy is provided. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; Progress and reporting tab; Questions: S521, S1243; Explanation of how the chosen scope 2 reduction strategy aligns with the selected scope 2 accounting approach. |

---

#### NT C9 — Scope 3 Inventory

**Criteria header:** NT C9 - Scope 3 inventory: Companies shall complete a scope 3 inventory covering gross scope 3 emissions for all its relevant emissions sources according to the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain (Scope 3) Accounting and Reporting Standard.*,**

*\* To determine relevance of scope 3 activities for inclusion in the target boundary, companies will be assessed against minimum boundary in Table 5.4 and using the criteria in Table 6.1 of the Corporate Value Chain (Scope 3) Accounting and Reporting Standard. Please note that, although beyond the minimum boundary, all transport-related emissions across all sectors must be reported on a well-to-wheel (WTW) basis in companies' GHG inventories (well-to-wake for aviation and maritime transport). All use-phase emissions from third-party distributed fossil fuels must be reported in scope 3 category 11 for all companies engaged in this type of distribution activity.*
*\*\* Companies may use the Partnership for Carbon Accounting Financials (PCAF) Global GHG Accounting and Reporting Standard for the Financial Industry to calculate financed emissions. However, emissions beyond the minimum requirements of the Greenhouse Gas Protocol for Scope 3 Category 15 Investments as per Table 5.9 (page 52) of the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain (Scope 3) Accounting and Reporting Standard shall not count towards the mandatory boundary for scope 3 targets (see C6 and C7). Companies may, however, set optional targets on these emissions.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **9.1 Scope 3 GHG accounting** | GHG Accounting | Companies must conduct a full scope 3 inventory and calculate emissions for each scope 3 category regardless of perceived relevance or magnitude. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Evaluation questions tab; Questions: S61 through S61522, R1333; Within the 'GHG Inventory - Scope 3' section of the portal, companies must report a figure for all scope 3 emissions categories in tCO₂e, write a detailed assumption and description of the emissions included in the category, and describe how these fit within the minimum boundaries prescribed by the GHG Protocol. Emissions from categories deemed immaterial must be quantified in tCO₂e and full descriptions must be provided. Companies may also upload supplemental documentation of the methodology/emissions factors used to derive the figures in the evaluation tab of the Validation Portal. |
| **9.2 SBTi scope 3 requirements** | GHG Accounting | Companies must adhere to all SBTi GHG Accounting expectations beyond the GHG Protocol Scope 3 Corporate Value Chain Standard. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General Questions; Questions: S321; Confirmation. Companies must confirm GHG accounting adheres to the SBTi GHG accounting Criteria Assessment Indicators GHG C3 - GHG C18, ensuring conformance with any additional SBTi GHG Accounting criteria. |
| **9.3 SBTi scope 3 Criteria** | GHG Accounting | GHG accounting must be in accordance with SBTi GHG accounting Criteria Assessment Indicators GHG C3 - GHG C18. | Demonstration of objective evidence needed for GHG Accounting Criteria Assessment Indicators GHG C3 - GHG C18. |
| **9.4 Scope 3 Market-Based GHG Accounting** | GHG Accounting | As per the Greenhouse Gas Protocol guidance, the SBTi does not permit market-based accounting in scope 3, including the purchase of market-based renewable electricity instruments on behalf of the reporting company's suppliers, customers, lessors, lessees, franchisees, or investments. Companies can report scope 3 emissions based on specific primary emissions data received from their suppliers, customers, lessors, lessees, franchisees or investments that are determined by those value chain partners using market-based GHG accounting. | Companies must confirm GHG accounting adheres to the SBTi GHG Accounting Criteria Assessment Indicators GHG C3 - GHG C18. |
| **9.5 Unrounded emissions** | GHG Accounting | GHG emissions must be reported on an unrounded basis. If rounding is necessary, figures must be rounded to the nearest whole number. Figures rounded to the nearest ten, hundred, thousand, etc. are unacceptable. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61; Within the 'GHG Inventory - Scope 3' section of the portal, all emissions reported in category specific breakdown tables must be unrounded or rounded to the nearest whole number. |

---

#### NT C10 — Biogenic Accounting

**Criteria header:** NT C10 – Biogenic accounting: Companies that use bioenergy or have biogenic emissions within their operations or value chain shall:
- Report CO₂ emissions and removals in line with GHG Protocol guidance.
- Include net* CO₂ emissions from biogenic sources in the target boundary for scopes 1, 2 and 3**, and track these net emissions when reporting progress against science-based targets.
- Include the required footnote in target language***: "The target boundary includes land-related emissions and removals from biogenic feedstocks."
- Report all upstream CO₂e emissions from bioenergy and biogenic feedstocks in the main GHG inventory. Upstream emissions must include: CO₂e from direct land use change**** (LUC); Non-LUC emissions, including N₂O and CH₄ from land management; CO₂e from processing and distribution.
- Follow any future GHG Protocol guidance on bioenergy accounting once released to maintain alignment with C11.

*\* Negative emissions due to biogenic removals shall not be accounted for in a company's target formulation or as progress towards SBTs. In addition, removals that are not directly associated with bioenergy feedstock production are not accepted to count as progress towards SBTs or to net emissions in a company's GHG inventory.*
*\*\* Biogenic scope 3 emissions must only be included if the net scope 3 coverage is below the minimum threshold.*
*\*\*\* Companies intending to use bioenergy or other biogenic emissions sources during the target timeframe must also include the required footnote in their target language.*
*\*\*\*\* Reporting emissions from indirect LUC is optional.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **10.1 Biogenic emissions allocation** | GHG Accounting | Companies using bioenergy or with biogenic emissions within their operations must report CO₂ emissions and removals associated with the biogenic feedstocks alongside the inventory, as per the guidance provided by GHG Protocol. Companies must report N₂O and CH₄ emissions within the main inventory in the relevant scope (and category). | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General Questions; Questions: S351, S3511, S3512, S3514; Companies must confirm they follow the GHG Protocol Guidance on biogenic emissions accounting and provide information on the methodology used to calculate the CO₂ emissions and removals. Corroborating data must be provided throughout the reported GHG inventory in the portal. |
| **10.2 Biogenic upstream emissions allocation** | GHG Accounting | Companies using bioenergy or with biogenic emissions within their operations must report the upstream emissions associated with processing and distribution, as well as the land-related emissions of the feedstock, in scope 3 category 3. Land-related emissions accounting must include CO₂ emissions from direct land use change (LUC) and non-LUC emissions, inclusive of N₂O and CH₄ emissions from land use management. Including emissions associated with indirect LUC is optional. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General Questions; Questions: S3517; Confirmation. |
| **10.3 Biogenic emissions in the value chain** | GHG Accounting | Companies with biogenic emissions sources within their value chain must report the CO₂ emissions and removals alongside the inventory's scope 3 category under which the activity would fall. For example, a paid transportation service conducted using a biofuel would have the combustion CO₂ emissions and the associated feedstock removals (TTW) reported alongside scope 3 category 4. The upstream emissions (WTT) associated with the feedstock, as well as CH₄ and N₂O combustion emissions would then be reported in the main inventory category 4. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General Questions; Questions: S351, S3511, S3512, S3514, S3515, S3517; Companies must confirm they follow the GHG Protocol Guidance on biogenic accounting and provide information on the methodology used to calculate the combustion CO₂ emissions from the consumed biogenic. Corroborating data must be provided throughout the reported GHG Inventory of the portal. |
| **10.4 Justifying biogenic emissions** | GHG Accounting | Companies with biogenic emissions must disclose the justifications/assumptions on the methods and renewability of the biogenic feedstocks. This will include assumptions on emission factors. Companies with biogenic emissions must also confirm that they will update their inventory if/when the SBTi endorses specific methods/factors for estimating these emissions and/or removals. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S3511, S3513, S52, S522, S61; Provision of details on the feedstock sources (e.g. biodiesel from palm oil, sugarcane ethanol, etc), and the methods used to calculate biogenic emissions/removals until an SBTi-endorsed method becomes available. Agreement to adjust these figures in the future. |
| **10.5 Including biogenic emissions in target boundaries** | Target Setting | Companies with biogenic emissions must clarify whether associated net emissions, including the net emissions from the combustion phase, are covered by eligible science-based targets. Biogenic emissions in a company's own operations (scopes 1 and 2) must be covered by targets, regardless of the magnitude of these emissions. Biogenic emissions coverage in scope 3 is only required if necessary to meet minimum coverage requirements across all scope 3 emissions as stated in NT C6. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term target; Companies must include biogenic emissions within the target boundaries according to near-term target coverage requirements NT C4 and NT C5, demonstrating adherence by entering emissions magnitudes for each target respectively that displays complete coverage of biogenic related emissions. |
| **10.6 Footnote usage** | Target Setting | For targets that cover activities giving rise to biogenic emissions, either net-positive or net-neutral, the reporting company's target language must include the following footnote: "*The target boundary includes land-related emissions and removals from biogenic feedstocks." | Acceptance to the biogenic footnote in the target language as generated in the Validation Portal. |

---

#### NT C11 — Carbon Credits

**Criteria header:** NT C11 - Carbon credits: The use of carbon credits must not be counted as emission reductions toward the progress of companies' near-term or long-term science-based targets. Carbon credits may only be considered as an option for neutralizing residual emissions (see Corporate Net-Zero Standard Criteria C28) or to finance additional climate mitigation beyond their science-based emission reduction targets (see Corporate Net-Zero Standard Criteria R9).

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **11.1 Carbon credits for target progress** | Target Setting | Reductions that result from the purchase of carbon credits must be reported outside of the main GHG inventory and tracked separately from validated targets. Carbon credits do not count toward the achievement of near or long-term targets, and companies must select a target ambition that is based on the reductions which can be achieved through direct mitigation levers. If companies choose to purchase carbon credits, these credits may be used for Beyond Value Chain Mitigation (BVCM), or for neutralization of residual emissions. | Portal Location: Progress and reporting tab; Question: S1241; Confirmation for the question that carbon credits (e.g. offsets) will not be counted toward target progress. |

---

#### NT C12 — Avoided Emissions

**Criteria header:** NT C12 - Avoided emissions: Avoided emissions fall under a separate accounting system from corporate inventories and do not count toward near-term science-based emission reduction targets.

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **12.1 Accounting and tracking of avoided emissions separately from GHG inventory and targets** | GHG Accounting | Companies must not report avoided emissions in their GHG inventory or count avoided emissions toward near or long-term target achievement. Companies wishing to track avoided emissions must account for these emissions under an entirely different accounting system outside of their science-based targets. | Portal Location: Progress and reporting tab; Question: S1242; Confirmation for the question that avoided emissions are not included in the GHG inventory calculations or covered by any proposed targets. |

---

#### NT C13 — Base and Target Years

**Criteria header:** NT C13 - Base and target years: Absolute and intensity-based emission reduction near-term targets must cover a minimum of 5 years and a maximum of 10 years from the date the target is submitted to the SBTi for validation. The choice of base year must be no earlier than 2015. Scope 1 and scope 2 targets must use the same base year.* The SBTi does not accept multi-year average base years, unless this is specified in the sector-guidance relevant to the company.

*\* Scope 3 targets are recommended but not required to use the same base year as scope 1 and scope 2 targets. Base years across different scope 3 targets must be the same.*
*\*R7 – 2030 target year: It is recommended that companies select a 2030 target year for all near-term targets. Applying this recommendation exempts a company from the 5-10 year timeframe requirement in C13.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **13.1 Near-term target timeframe** | Target Setting | Targets must cover a minimum of 5 years and a maximum of 10 years from the date of submission. It is recommended companies use the same base year and most recent year when reporting greenhouse gas inventories to the SBTi, but, if necessary, companies may report a different year for scope 3 when compared to scope 1 and 2. The scope 1 base year must be the same as the scope 2 base year as well as the most recent year. Within scope 3, the base year must also be consistent across all categories. The scope 3 most recent year must also be consistent across all categories. | Portal Location: Targets Tab - Add near-term target; Question: S11113 for cross-sector targets; Selection of a target year in the targets tab of the Validation Portal that adheres to NT 13.1 for all the targets. |
| **13.2 Consistent base year for targets with different timeframes** | Target Setting | Once companies select a base year, that base year must be used consistently for both near-term and long-term target setting for targets of the same scope. | Portal Location: Targets Tab - Add near-term target; The selected base year displayed in the targets tab of the Validation Portal that adheres to NT 13.2 for all the targets. |
| **13.3 Base year choice** | Target Setting | Base years must cover a complete past calendar or financial year. Companies must set targets with a base year of 2015 or later. Any companies that used base years prior to 2015 during past SBTi submissions must update their base year to 2015 or later during the target resubmission process. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Reporting years; Questions: S212, S216; Submission of base year inventory in validation portal that adheres to NT 13.3. |
| **13.4 Combined scope target base years** | Target Setting | Companies setting targets covering scope 1 and/or 2 and scope 3 must use the same base year for the scope 3 portion as for the scope 1 and 2 portion of the GHG inventory. This applies to cross-sector absolute reduction targets as well as sector-specific intensity convergence targets. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Reporting years; Questions: S216; Selection of consistent base year for the scope 1 and 2 portion of the targets and scope 3 portion of the targets in the validation portal. |
| **13.5 Selection of 2030 as target year** | Target Setting | Companies that select the recommended 2030 target year for their near-term target shall be exempt from the minimum 5 year timeframe requirement detailed in NT C13.1.** *\*\* R7– 2030 target year: It is recommended that companies select a 2030 target year for all near-term targets. Applying this recommendation exempts a company from the 5-10 year timeframe requirement in C13.* | Portal Location: Targets Tab - Add near-term target; Question: S11113 for cross-sector targets. |

---

#### NT C14 — Progress to Date

**Criteria header:** NT C14 - Progress to date: The minimum forward-looking ambition of near-term targets covering scope 1 and/or scope 2 emissions is consistent with reaching net-zero by 2050 at the latest, assuming a linear absolute reduction, linear intensity reduction, or intensity convergence between the most recent year and 2050 (not increasing absolute emissions or intensity).*,**

*\* The most recent year used for scope 1 and scope 2 emissions shall be the same year. The most recent year used for scope 3 emissions is recommended to be the same year as scope 1 and scope 2.*
*\*\* Companies shall provide all the relevant GHG inventory data including a most recent year GHG inventory. For submissions in 2026, the most recent inventory shall be no earlier than 2024 i.e. allowable most recent years are 2024 and 2025. Companies should also note that applying proxy data (i.e., applying one reporting year's data to another reporting year) is not permitted. For example, a company may not apply base-year emissions to the most recent year.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **14.1 Provision of most recent year GHG inventory** | GHG Accounting | The most recent GHG inventory provided must be for a complete year, and must be no earlier than 2 years prior to the date of submission. For submissions in 2025, a recent year inventory must be provided that is no earlier than 2023, i.e., allowable most recent years are 2023 and 2024. When a company uses fiscal years in its GHG accounting, the SBTi assesses based on the calendar year (CY) where the majority of the months occur. E.g. FY2022 with a date range of April 2021 - March 2022 would be assessed as CY2021. In the rare case where a FY is evenly split across a CY (i.e. FY ends on 30th June), the year is assessed using the later year in the date range. This approach is applicable to all targets. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Reporting years; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; S212, S52, S522, S61; Confirmation and description of key scope 1, 2 and 3 business activities alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes for the most recent year. |
| **14.2 Use of SBTi target setting tool** | Target Setting | The SBTi target setting tool, now embedded in the portal, must be used to calculate the minimum ambition of near-term scope 1 and/or scope 2 targets including the most recent year emissions. For companies using the most recent year as a base year, this section is not relevant and does not affect minimum target ambition. | Portal Location: Targets Tab - Add near-term target; Questions: S11119; Results of the validation portal calculation based on related inputs proves the company's conformance with this indicator. |
| **14.3 Assessment of intensity forward looking ambition** | Target Setting | If the target is intensity-based, the criterion is met if: Company activities align with the requirements of the SDA guidance (if applicable) and pathway. See Sector-Specific Requirements Table 1 in the SBTi near-term criteria for further information. Ambition is at a minimum, aligned with reaching the net-zero convergence intensity based on a linear intensity reduction between the most recent year and 2050. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term target (Absolute cross sector or sector-specific target); Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. Companies must select at least the minimum ambition calculated within the Validation Portal when setting a target(s) or the target ambition specified by the relevant SBTi target setting tool if a sector specific target has been set and a tool is required to be uploaded. |
| **14.4 Assessment of target achievement** | Target Setting | Target has not been achieved with the most recent year GHG inventory provided. | Portal location: Targets tab - Add near-term target; Companies must select at least the minimum ambition in the Validation Portal when setting a target, or the ambition specified by the corresponding SBTi target setting tool if a sector specific target has been set and a tool is required to be uploaded. Companies must also ensure the target has not been achieved as per the most recent year inventory submitted. |

---

| **14.5 Assessment of most recent year representativeness** | GHG Accounting | Companies must provide all the relevant GHG inventory data including a most recent year GHG inventory even if business activities were impacted by the COVID-19 pandemic. If any years subsequent to the base year are unrepresentative, companies must explain why, and indicate the rationale for the choice of the most recent year. The achievement of near-term target(s) due to COVID-19 pandemic impacts on the levels of business activity does not apply unless evidence is submitted quantitatively demonstrating how activities are returning to pre-COVID levels. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Overview; Evaluation questions tab; Questions: S741, R1333; Confirmation and upload of a supporting document as quantitative evidence. |

---

#### NT C15 — Level of Ambition for Scope 1 and 2 Targets

**Criteria header:** NT C15 - Level of ambition for scope 1 and 2 targets: At a minimum, scope 1 and scope 2 targets shall be consistent with the level of decarbonization required to keep global temperature increase to 1.5°C compared to pre-industrial temperatures.*

*\* When a company uses fiscal years in its GHG accounting, the SBTi assesses minimum ambition based on the calendar year (CY) where the majority of the months occur. E.g. FY2022 with a date range of April 2021 - March 2022 would be assessed as CY2021. In the rare case where a FY is evenly split across a CY (i.e. FY ends on 30th June), ambition is assessed using the later year in the date range. This approach is applicable to all targets.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **15.1 Assessment of absolute contraction ambition** | Target Setting | If the target is absolute-based, the criterion is met if companies are in conformance with SBTi Near-Term Criterion 16. | Demonstration of minimum documentation required for NT C16. |
| **15.2 Assessment of intensity ambition** | Target Setting | If the target is intensity-based, the criterion is met if companies are in conformance with SBTi Near-Term Criterion 17. | Demonstration of minimum documentation required for NT C17. |
| **15.3 Assessment of renewable electricity procurement ambition** | Target Setting | For renewable electricity procurement targets, the criterion is met if the companies are in conformance with SBTi Near-Term Criterion 21. | Demonstration of minimum documentation required for NT C21. |

---

#### NT C16 — Absolute Targets

**Criteria header:** NT C16 - Absolute targets: Absolute reduction targets for scope 1 and scope 2 are eligible when they are at least as ambitious as the minimum of the approved range of emissions scenarios consistent with the 1.5°C goal.

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **16.1 Assessment of ambition after 2020** | Target Setting | For base years after 2020, the absolute emissions reduction must meet the minimum reduction value over the target period as set out below: Minimum value for absolute reduction target = 4.2% x (Target year - 2020). | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Absolute cross sector; Questions: S11114, S11119; Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. Companies must select at least the minimum ambition calculated within the Validation Portal when setting target(s). |
| **16.2 Assessment of ambition before 2020** | Target Setting | For base years between 2015 and 2020 (inclusive), the absolute emissions reduction must meet the minimum reduction value over the target period as set out below: Minimum value for absolute reduction target = 4.2% x (Target year - base year). | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Absolute cross sector; Questions: S11114, S11119; Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. Companies must select at least the minimum ambition calculated within the Validation Portal when setting target(s). |

---

#### NT C17 — Intensity Targets

**Criteria header:** NT C17 - Intensity targets: Intensity targets for scope 1 and scope 2 emissions are only eligible when they are modeled using an approved 1.5°C sector pathway applicable to companies' business activities.

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **17.1 Assessment of intensity ambition** | Target Setting | The SDA pathway must be representative of company activities and the ambition between the base year and target year must be aligned with the minimum ambition threshold of the relevant 1.5°C SDA pathway. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Overview; Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target; Questions: S731; Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. Companies must select at least the minimum ambition calculated within the Validation Portal when setting SDA target(s) or otherwise the minimum ambition displayed within the corresponding SBTi target setting tool if a tool is required to be uploaded. |

---

#### NT C18 — Level of Ambition for Scope 3 Emissions Reductions Targets

**Criteria header:** NT C18 - Level of ambition for scope 3 emissions reductions targets: At a minimum, near-term scope 3 targets (covering total required scope 3 emissions or individual scope 3 categories) shall be aligned with methods consistent with the level of decarbonization required to keep global temperature increase well-below 2°C compared to pre-industrial temperatures.*

*\* When a company uses fiscal years in its GHG accounting, the SBTi assesses minimum ambition based on the calendar year (CY) where the majority of the months occur. E.g. FY2022 with a date range of April 2021 - March 2022 would be assessed as CY2021. In the rare case where a FY is evenly split across a CY (ie FY ends on 30th June), ambition is assessed using the later year in the date range. This approach is applicable to all targets.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **18.1 Assessment of absolute ambition after 2020** | Target Setting | For base years 2020 or later, the timeframe ambition (i.e., ambition from the base year to the target year) for absolute percentage-based emission reduction targets must be, at a minimum, aligned with the well-below 2°C ambition threshold. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Absolute cross sector; Questions: S11114, S11119; Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. Companies must select at least the minimum ambition calculated within the Validation Portal when setting target(s). |
| **18.2 Assessment of absolute ambition before 2020** | Target Setting | For base years between 2015 and 2020 inclusive, the timeframe ambition (i.e., ambition from the base year to the target year) for absolute percentage-based emission reduction targets must be, at a minimum, aligned with the well-below 2°C ambition threshold. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Absolute cross sector; Questions: S11114, S11119; Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. Companies must select at least the minimum ambition in the Validation Portal when setting target(s). |
| **18.3 Assessment of economic intensity metric** | Target Setting | If the target is based on reduction of economic intensity, the economic intensity metric must be based on greenhouse gas emissions per unit of value added (GEVA). The calculations of value added must use the formulae set out in "Greenhouse gas emissions per unit of value added ("GEVA") — A corporate guide to voluntary climate action": Value added = gross profit; Value added = operating profit = earnings before interest and depreciation (EBITDA) + all personnel costs (personnel costs must include payment to management and board members); Value added = sales revenue - the cost of goods and services purchased from external suppliers. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - GEVA: Economic Intensity; Questions: S11116, S111161; Company must select one of the GEVA-approved metrics detailed in the Validation Portal as well as in NT 18.3. |
| **18.4 Assessment of physical or economic intensity growth** | Target Setting | If the target is based on reduction of physical or economic intensity, the intensity targets must be paired with relevant, credible and justifiable activity growth projections. If activity projections are updated during the target timeframe, refer to NT C26 and NT C27. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - GEVA: Economic Intensity; Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Physical Intensity; Questions: S11117, S111171, S111172, S111173, S111174; Confirmation of activity in base year and target year, along with uploading any documents to substantiate the growth projections considered for setting the target. |
| **18.5 Assessment of physical intensity metric** | Target Setting | Physical intensity denominator must be representative of the reporting company's emissions in the target boundary, corresponding to a measurable product, output, level or service. It cannot be a unit of monetary or economic value. Companies are required to provide a clear definition of the physical intensity unit applied in this type of target, and a justification for why the proposed activity unit corresponds to the company's business trajectory. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Physical Intensity; Questions: S111152, S111153; Companies must indicate a chosen metric for the physical intensity target and justify the reasoning for its selection, uploading any documents to support the reasoning. |
| **18.6 Comparison of physical intensity and SDA** | Target Setting | Scope 3 SDA intensity convergence targets are intensity targets that are based on physical activity indicators. However, these targets are not to be assessed by the minimum ambition requirements of the physical intensity target setting method. Companies that choose to use intensity methods must ensure their intensity targets meet or exceed the minimum ambition requirements of the corresponding SDA pathway. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add target; If an SDA pathway is available, the physical intensity timeframe ambition must be aligned with the minimum ambition threshold of the relevant SDA pathway at a minimum. For sectors where an SDA is required or selected, the minimum ambition threshold for SDA targets must therefore also be in line with the corresponding SBTi target setting tool. |
| **18.7 Assessment of physical or economic intensity ambition from 2020** | Target Setting | For base years 2020 or later, intensity-based emission reduction targets the timeframe ambition (i.e., ambition from the base year to the target year) must be, at a minimum, aligned with the well-below 2°C ambition threshold. Targets must drive ambitious physical or economic intensity reduction to lead to at least a 7% intensity reduction in annual compounded terms. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - GEVA: Economic Intensity; Questions: S11119, S111191; Minimum value for physical or economic intensity target = 100% - (93%)^(Target year - 2020); Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. Companies must at least select the minimum ambition calculated within the validation portal when setting intensity based targets. |
| **18.8 Assessment of physical or economic intensity ambition before 2020** | Target Setting | For base years between 2015 and 2020 inclusive, intensity-based emission reduction targets the timeframe ambition (i.e., ambition from the base year to the target year) must be, at a minimum, aligned with the well-below 2°C ambition threshold. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - GEVA: Economic Intensity; Questions: S11119, S111191; Minimum value for physical or economic intensity target = 100% - (93%)^(Target year - base year); Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. Companies must at least select the minimum ambition calculated within the Validation Portal when setting intensity based targets. |
| **18.9 Beyond minimum boundary** | Target Setting | For companies wishing to report and target emissions beyond the minimum boundary in scope 3, the ambition of the optional emissions target must be, at a minimum, aligned with the well-below 2°C ambition threshold. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term beyond minimum boundary target; Questions: S117110; Results of validation portal calculation based on related inputs, that proves company's conformance with this indicator. Companies must at least select the minimum ambition calculated within the Validation Portal when setting this target. |

---

#### NT C19 — Supplier or Customer Engagement Targets

**Criteria header:** NT C19 - Supplier or customer engagement targets: Near-term targets to drive the adoption of science-based emission reduction targets by their corporate suppliers and/or customers shall meet the following requirements:
- Boundary: Companies may set engagement targets across upstream or downstream scope 3 categories.
- Formulation: Companies shall provide information in the target language on what percentage of emissions from relevant upstream and/or downstream categories is covered by the engagement target or, if that information is not available, what percentage of annual procurement spend is covered by the target.*
- Timeframe: Engagement targets shall be fulfilled within a maximum of 5 years from the date the company's target is submitted to the SBTi for validation.
- Ambition level: The company's suppliers/customers shall have science-based emission reduction targets in line with the latest version of the SBTi Criteria for Near-term Targets.

*\* If measuring coverage by spend, the company shall provide an estimate of the emissions coverage associated with that spend for validation purposes to demonstrate that criterion C6 has been met, by the supplier or customer target alone or together with other scope 3 target(s).*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **19.1 Assessment of engagement target boundary** | Target Setting | The supplier/customer engagement target boundary must correspond only to the emissions associated with the suppliers/customers within the target boundary. It is not possible for an engagement target to cover 100% of a category unless the company intends to engage 100% of suppliers/customers giving rise to emissions within that category. The portion of suppliers/customers that are covered by the target and how much they represent in overall emissions must be disclosed. This may be demonstrated by supplying information on the group, percentage, or product/service related to the suppliers/customers that will be covered by the target. Companies must only set supplier or customer engagement targets over categories where suppliers/customers are eligible to set SBTs, and for which the company is able to directly engage with the entities responsible for that category's emissions. Customer engagement targets must only be set over business customers. Business-to-consumer (B2C) activities are not eligible to be included in an engagement target. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Supplier/Customer Engagement; Questions: S11114, S111141, S111110, S1111101, S1111108, S1111109; Percentage of emissions and the portion of suppliers or customers the target covers in relevant categories disclosed in the targets tab of the SBTi validation portal. |
| **19.2 Assessment of spend proxy** | Target Setting | Companies may use a "per spend" proxy but must provide an estimate of the emissions coverage associated with that spend to demonstrate that engagement target requirements are met. If using a "per spend" proxy, the percentage covered must only correspond to the spend on suppliers or revenue generated from sales to customers in the desired scope 3 categories of the target coverage. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Supplier/Customer Engagement; Questions: S111110, S1111101, S1111102; Provision of the absolute emissions the "per spend" proxy covers in the targets tab of the SBTi validation portal and justification of how spend/revenue has been converted to emissions. |
| **19.3 Assessment of engagement target timeframe** | Target Setting | The submitting company's engagement target year, by which engaged suppliers' targets must be set, shall be within 5 years (inclusive) from the date of submission. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Supplier/Customer Engagement; Questions: S11113; The target year entered in the targets tab of the validation portal is a maximum of 5 years from the date the target is submitted for validation. |
| **19.4 Assessment of engagement target plan** | Target Setting | A high-level plan of supplier/customer engagement must also be included within the submission form including the portion of suppliers/customers covered by the target. Engagement targets on downstream customers may be set, but companies must also disclose how it can credibly influence these customers to set their own targets. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Supplier/Customer Engagement; Questions: S1111103, S1111104, S1111105, S1111106; Written explanation demonstrating the company has considerable influence over suppliers or customers included in the engagement target and ability to track supplier engagement target progress over time. |
| **19.5 Assessment of engagement emission boundary** | Target Setting | If suppliers/customers are only required to set SBTs on certain scopes, only those scopes of emissions must be accounted for in the boundary. The scopes of emissions requiring targeting by the suppliers/customers and the minimum coverage requirements of such targets are set out in NT criteria 3, 4, 6 and 22 or relevant sectoral guidance. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Supplier/Customer Engagement; Questions: S1111108, S1111109; Disclosure of the portion of targeted emissions corresponding to suppliers/customers with SBTs and of supplier engagement target ambition. |
| **19.6 Criteria version for engagement targets** | Target Setting | Supplier/customer engagement targets are required to be set in accordance with the latest version of the SBTi Corporate Near-Term Criteria. Official validation of suppliers' targets by the SBTi is not required, though companies are welcome to encourage this if they wish. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Supplier/Customer Engagement; Companies accept the auto generated target wording generated in the Validation Portal and requirements indicating that their suppliers/customers will set science-based targets that meet the latest version SBTi Corporate Near-term Criteria. |
| **19.7 Eligible coverage for engagement targets** | Target Setting | Companies setting customer engagement targets over category 11 must plan to engage business customers. Companies may not set category 11 engagement targets over emissions from individual consumers. Companies must only set supplier or customer engagement targets over scope 3 emissions sources which are credible for the company to engage with. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Supplier/Customer Engagement; Portal Location: Progress and reporting tab; Questions: S1111103, S1111104, S1111105, S1111106, S1111108, S1111109, S1245; The target language and target coverage entered in the Validation Portal shall reflect the categories that are covered and companies must explain the credible engagement they can have within these categories when describing their company's scope 3 reduction strategy. |
| **19.8 Target formulation** | Target Setting | The target language shall include the percent coverage of categories within the target boundary, rather than the percent coverage of total scope 3 emissions. If coverage varies per category, the target language shall display a weighted average coverage of the emissions in the categories within the target boundary. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Supplier/Customer Engagement; Questions: S1111108, S1111109; Companies shall enter the correct proportion of targeted emissions in the base year, most recent year, and target year and accept the auto generated target wording generated in the Validation Portal. |

---

#### NT C20 — Combined Scope Targets

**Criteria header:** NT C20 - Combined scope targets: Targets that combine scopes (e.g., 1+2 or 1+2+3) are permitted if the SBTi can review the ambition of the individual target components and confirm each meets the relevant ambition criteria.*

*\* When submitting combined near-term targets, the scope 1+2 portion must be in line with at least a 1.5°C scenario and the scope 3 portion of the target must be in line with at least a well-below 2°C scenario. For sectors where minimum target ambition is further specified for companies' scope 3 activities, C24 supersedes C20.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **20.1 Superseded criterion** | Target Setting | For sectors where minimum target ambition is further specified for companies' scope 3 activities, C24 supersedes C20. | Demonstration of objective evidence needed for NT C24. |
| **20.2 Assessment of combined scope 1 and 2 target** | Target Setting | Targets combining scope 1 and 2 must be in line with the ambition criteria C14 and C15. If submitting a combined scope 1 and 2 target, reductions in both scopes must be made. | Demonstration of objective evidence that the combined scope 1 and 2 portion is in line with NT C14 and NT C15. |
| **20.3 Assessment of combined scope 1, 2 and 3 target** | Target Setting | For targets combining scope 1, 2 and 3, the scope 1 and 2 portion of the target must be in line with criteria C14 and C15 and the scope 3 portion must be in line with criterion C18. | Demonstration of objective evidence that the combined scope 1 and 2 ambition is in line with NT C14 and NT C15 and the scope 3 portion is in line with NT C18. |
| **20.4 Reduction compensation within a combined target** | Measurement, reporting and verification | Compensation of reductions between targets set over scopes 1+2 and scope 3 must not occur. Targets are modeled, measured, tracked, and therefore also achieved, at a disaggregated level. | Confirmation of disaggregated ambition as per inputs to the targets tab of the SBTi Validation Portal where a scope 1 and 2 target must be listed separately from scope 3. |
| **20.5 Base years for combined targets** | Target setting | For targets combining scope 1 and/or 2 and 3, the base year for all scopes must be consistent. This criterion supersedes NT C13.1. | Scope 3 base year is confirmed to be consistent with scope 1 and 2 base year as per autogenerated target language displayed in targets tab of the SBTi Validation Portal. |

---

#### NT C21 — Renewable Electricity (Scope 2 Only)

**Criteria header:** NT C21 - Renewable electricity (scope 2 only): Targets to actively source renewable electricity* at a rate consistent with 1.5°C scenarios are an acceptable alternative to scope 2 emission reduction targets*. The SBTi has identified 80% renewable electricity procurement by 2025 and 100% by 2030 as thresholds (portion of renewable electricity over total electricity use) for this approach, in line with the recommendations of RE100**. Companies that already source electricity at or above these thresholds shall maintain or increase their use of renewable electricity to qualify. For long-term targets, companies shall maintain 100% active renewable electricity procurement beyond 2030.

*\* Companies reporting scope 2 emissions using location-based methods can still set a renewable electricity target provided they have the capacity to demonstrate active sourcing of renewable electricity through market instruments.*
*\*\* RE100 guidance states that setting a 100% renewable electricity target by 2030 at the latest shows a strong level of leadership.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **21.1 Assessment of RE procurement** | Target Setting | The share of renewable electricity in the base year and most recent year must be calculated using the definitions of renewable electricity in GHG Protocol Scope 2 Guidance. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Renewable Electricity Procurement; Questions: S11118, S111181; Disclosure of the share of renewable electricity in base year and most recent year within the Validation Portal. |
| **21.2 Assessment of renewable electricity ambition** | Target Setting | Targets with a target year between 2025 and 2030 will be accepted if they meet the linear progression of these requirements: 84% by 2026; 88% by 2027; 92% by 2028; or 96% by 2029. Companies that are already actively sourcing renewable electricity at or above the minimum thresholds must commit to maintain or increase their share of renewable electricity to qualify for a renewable electricity target. For instance, a company at 99% procurement that has set targets to reach 100% procurement by 2025 would be required to set a 100% RE maintenance target through 2030 rather than being able to target a reduced renewable percentage. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term cross sector target - Renewable Electricity Procurement; Questions: S11119, S111191; The active sourcing of renewable electricity in the target year provided is at or above the minimum share thresholds. |
