#### GHG C12 — Suitable GHG Accounting Scope 3 Category 10: Processing of Sold Products

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **12.1 Conformity to GHG Protocol minimum boundary** | GHG Accounting | In category 10, companies must include all emissions associated with third-party processing of intermediate products sold in the reporting year, in conformance with Table 5.4 of the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard. Companies are expected to account for all downstream scope 3 categories from intermediate products and services, where relevant. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6101, S61012, S61013; Provision of details on the company's relevant activities with emissions in category 10, with a breakdown of emission sources. |
| **12.2 Definition of intermediate products** | GHG Accounting | In conformance with Box 5.3 of the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard, intermediate products are defined as "inputs to the production of other goods or services that require further processing, transformation, or inclusion in another product before use by the end consumer. Intermediate products are not consumed by the end user in their current form." Therefore, if companies sell goods that are defined as intermediate products, they must include all processing emissions in category 10. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6101, S61012, S61013; Confirmation of applicability. |
| **12.3 Calculation methods** | GHG Accounting | Companies must use calculation methods consistent with the GHG Protocol Technical Guidance for Calculating Scope 3 emissions. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61013; Provision of details of calculation methods. |
| **12.4 Applicability to intermediate products** | GHG Accounting | When the reporting company's sold goods are intermediate products, companies must include emissions associated with the processing allocated to the intermediate product. For any intermediate products whose final applications are known, companies are expected to report the emissions associated with processing either using data collected from customers or using publicly available product level or sector specific emissions factors. The applicability of category 10 must be evaluated for each intermediate product sold. When the end use is unknown, companies shall provide detailed justification. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6101, S61012, S61013; Reasonable justification of any unknown end use(s). |

---

#### GHG C13 — Suitable GHG Accounting Scope 3 Category 11: Use of Sold Products

*(From the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard page 48: This category includes emissions from the use of goods and services sold by the reporting company in the reporting year.)*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **13.1 Conformity to GHG Protocol minimum boundary** | GHG Accounting | In category 11, companies must include all emissions associated with the end use of goods and services sold by the reporting company in the reporting year, in conformance with Table 5.4 of the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard. The SBTi reserves the right to question the applicability or non-applicability of this criterion based on the organization's definition of use of sold service. Companies are expected to account for all downstream scope 3 categories from intermediate products and services, where relevant. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6111, S61112, S61113; Provision of details on the company's relevant activities with emissions in category 11, with a breakdown of emission sources. |
| **13.2 Reporting of WTW emissions** | GHG Accounting | For any sold vehicles, including but not limited to freight and passenger cars and trucks, trains, aircraft, and ships, companies must report use-phase emissions on a WTW basis, in conformance with Table 1 in the SBTi Criteria and Recommendations for Near-Term Targets. This requirement also covers automotive components with direct use-phase emissions. All other sold products must be reported on a TTW basis. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61123; Confirmation, alongside a breakdown of emission sources. |
| **13.3 Fossil fuels combustion** | GHG Accounting | For any sold fossil fuels, companies must report TTW emissions from the combustion phase in category 11. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6113, S61131, S61132; Confirmation. If companies sell other goods with use-phase emissions, the split between fossil fuel combustion and all other use-phase emissions must be provided. |
| **13.4 Disaggregation of optional emissions** | GHG Accounting | Companies must report optional emissions, e.g. indirect use-phase emissions, separately from the main category 11 emissions, as they are beyond the GHG Protocol minimum boundary. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61118, S611181; Confirmation of any optional boundary emissions. |
| **13.5 Calculation methods** | GHG Accounting | Companies must use calculation methods consistent with the GHG Protocol Technical Guidance for Calculating Scope 3 emissions. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61113; Provision of details of calculation methods. |
| **13.6 Applicability to intermediate products** | GHG Accounting | When the reporting company's sold goods are intermediate products, two scenarios may arise: 1. If the end use(s) of intermediate products is known, companies must include direct use-phase emissions of the intermediate products. 2. If the end use(s) of the intermediate product is unknown, companies may exclude emissions associated with the use-phase of the intermediate products. When the end use(s) is unknown, the companies must provide reasonable justification. Companies are expected to account for all downstream scope 3 categories from intermediate products and services, where relevant. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61113; Provision of breakdown of category 11 emissions. Reasonable justification of any unknown end use(s). |

| **13.7 Sold services** | GHG Accounting | Companies that sell services as a primary or secondary part of their business shall report category 11 emissions linked to the use-phase of the sold services. Examples include but are not limited to emissions from travel booked on behalf of customers, emissions from property management services, and emissions arising from certain types of booking platform arrangements. Companies including sold services in the target boundary that have less direct influence over category 11 emissions may wish to employ supplier or customer engagement as their target setting method. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6111, S61112, S61113, S6114, S61141; Confirmation that sold services emissions are included in reporting. Provision of details on the company's relevant activities with emissions in category 11, with a breakdown of emission sources. |

---

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **14.1 Inclusion of fossil fuel combustion** | GHG Accounting | For companies involved in the transmission or distribution of fossil fuels, companies must report TTW emissions from the combustion phase of those third-party owned fuels in category 11. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6113, S61131, S61132; Provision of breakdown of fossil fuels transmitted or distributed by the reporting company in the reporting year. If companies sell other goods with use-phase emissions, the split between fossil fuel combustion and all other use-phase emissions must be provided. |
| **14.2 Calculation methods** | GHG Accounting | Companies must use calculation methods consistent with the GHG Protocol Technical Guidance for Calculating Scope 3 emissions. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61113, S61132; Provision of details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material. |

#### GHG C15 — Suitable GHG Accounting Scope 3 Category 12: End-of-Life Treatment of Sold Products

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **15.1 Conformity to GHG Protocol minimum boundary** | GHG Accounting | In category 12, companies must include all emissions associated with the waste disposal and treatment of products sold by the reporting company (in the reporting year) at the end of their life, in conformance with Table 5.4 of the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard. Waste treatment activities applicable to category 12 include: Disposal in a landfill; Disposal in a landfill with landfill-gas-to-energy (LFGTE) -that is, combustion of landfill gas to generate electricity; Recovery for recycling; Incineration; Composting; Waste-to-energy (WTE) or energy-from-waste (EfW) -that is, combustion of municipal solid waste (MSW) to generate electricity; Wastewater treatment. Companies are expected to account for all downstream scope 3 categories from intermediate products and services, where relevant. In the instance that a company faces barriers to calculating emissions from one category of scope 3, the company shall demonstrate its best efforts to calculate these emissions, and this shall not preclude them from providing an estimate of emissions in other categories. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6121, S61212, S61213; Provision of details on the company's relevant activities with emissions in category 12, with a breakdown of emission sources. |
| **15.2 Disclosure of methodological assumptions** | GHG Accounting | The assumptions within the methodology for calculating emissions from the end of life treatment of sold products must be disclosed and reasonably justified. At a minimum, this must include the proportion of this waste being treated by different methods (e.g., percent landfilled, incinerated, recycled), broken down by key material or product type. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61213; Provision of details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material. |
| **15.3 Confirmation of completeness** | GHG Accounting | Companies must include in this category the emissions from disposal of any goods sold and any packaging associated with the sale. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6121, S61212, S61213; Provision of details on the company's relevant activities with emissions in category 12, with a breakdown of emission sources. |
| **15.4 Calculation methods** | GHG Accounting | Companies must use calculation methods consistent with the GHG Protocol Technical Guidance for Calculating Scope 3 emissions. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61213; Provision of details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material. |
| **15.5 Applicability to intermediate products** | GHG Accounting | When the reporting company's sold goods are intermediate products, two scenarios may arise: 1. If the end use(s) of the intermediate product is known, companies must include emissions associated with disposal of the intermediate products; 2. If the end use(s) of the intermediate product is unknown, companies may exclude emissions associated with the disposal of the intermediate products. When the end use(s) is unknown, companies must provide reasonable justification. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61213; Provision of breakdown of category 12 emissions. Reasonable justification of any unknown end use(s). |

---

#### GHG C16 — Suitable GHG Accounting Scope 3 Category 13: Downstream Leased Assets

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **16.1 Conformity to GHG Protocol minimum boundary** | GHG Accounting | In category 13, companies must include all emissions associated with the operation of assets owned by the reporting company (lessor) and leased to other entities in the reporting year, not included in scope 1 and scope 2 reported by the lessor, in conformance with Table 5.4 of the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6131, S61312, S61313; Provision of details on the company's relevant activities with emissions in category 13, with a breakdown of emission sources. |
| **16.2 Disaggregation of optional emissions** | GHG Accounting | Companies must report optional emissions, e.g. those associated with the life cycle emissions associated with manufacturing or constructing leased assets, separately from the main category 13 emissions, as they are beyond the GHG Protocol minimum boundary. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61318, S613181; Provision of a breakdown of optional emissions, alongside details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material. |
| **16.3 Calculation methods** | GHG Accounting | Companies must use calculation methods consistent with the GHG Protocol Technical Guidance for Calculating Scope 3 emissions. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61313; Provision of details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material. |
| **16.4 Allocation of downstream leased assets** | GHG Accounting | Companies shall align the allocation of emissions associated with upstream leased assets to Table [A.2] of the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard, unless reasonable justification is provided. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61312, S61321 - S61327; Provision of justification for reporting emissions within category 13. |

#### GHG C17 — Suitable GHG Accounting Scope 3 Category 14: Franchises

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **17.1 Conformity to GHG Protocol minimum boundary** | GHG Accounting | In category 14, companies must include all emissions associated with the operation of franchises in the reporting year, not included in scope 1 and scope 2 reported by franchisor, in conformance with Table 5.4 of the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard. The SBTi will assess the degree to which there are potential emissions reductions that could be undertaken or influenced by the company among their franchisees, to determine which franchise emissions should be included within the inventory boundary in accordance with GHG Principles. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6141, S61412, S61413, S61421, S61422, S61423; Provision of details on the company's relevant activities with emissions in category 14, with a breakdown of emission sources. |
| **17.2 Inclusion of licensing** | GHG Accounting | Companies who grant licenses to other entities to sell or distribute goods or services in return for payments, must account in this category for any scope 1 and 2 emissions arising from the creation or provision of those goods and services. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61424, S61425; Confirmation, and provision of details of the company's licensing agreements. |
| **17.3 Disaggregation of optional emissions** | GHG Accounting | Companies must report optional emissions, e.g. those associated with the life cycle emissions associated with manufacturing or constructing franchises, separately from the main category 14 emissions, as they are beyond the GHG Protocol minimum boundary. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61418, S614181; Provision of a breakdown of optional emissions, alongside details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material. |
| **17.4 Calculation methods** | GHG Accounting | Companies must use calculation methods consistent with the GHG Protocol Technical Guidance for Calculating Scope 3 emissions. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61413; Provision of details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material. |
| **17.5 Procurement** | GHG Accounting | Companies who procure goods and services on behalf of their franchises must report the relevant upstream and downstream emissions of those goods and services in respective scope 3 categories. Companies who do not procure goods and services for their franchises, but who have significant influence over their franchises' purchases, may choose to report the relevant upstream and downstream emissions from these purchases in respective scope 3 categories. Influence over purchases includes but is not limited to setting procurement policies for franchises, requiring franchises to use approved suppliers, or operating a centralized procurement system. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61423; Disclosure of purchasing arrangements with franchises. |

---

#### GHG C18 — Suitable GHG Accounting Scope 3 Category 15: Investments

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **18.1 Conformity to GHG Protocol minimum boundary** | GHG Accounting | Companies that are not financial institutions must report investments emissions in alignment with GHGP Scope 3 Guidance requirements: "Category 15 is designed primarily for private financial institutions (e.g., commercial banks), but is also relevant to public financial institutions (e.g., multilateral development banks, export credit agencies, etc.) and other entities with investments not included in scope 1 and scope 2." In category 15, companies must include all emissions associated with the operation of investments (according to GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard Table 5.9) in the reporting year, not included in scope 1 or scope 2 in conformance with Table 5.4 of the GHG Protocol Corporate Value Chain Standard. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S6151, S61512, S61513, S61521; Provision of details on the company's relevant activities with emissions in category 15, with a breakdown of emission sources. |
| **18.2 Inclusion of non-consolidated entities** | GHG Accounting | Scope 1 and 2 emissions of all joint ventures, assets, subsidiaries, and other equity holdings that are wholly or partially owned by the reporting company and that fall outside of the reporting company's selected consolidation approach must be included in this category proportionate to the reporting company's equity share in each entity or asset, in conformance with the GHG Protocol Technical Guidance for Calculating Scope 3 Emissions. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: R335111, S615181; Completion of the "Company structure templat.csv" file with details of percentage ownership of the reporting company and all worldwide subsidiaries, joint ventures, equity holdings, and other entities, and upload of the completed file. Provision of details on the company's relevant activities with emissions in category 15, with a breakdown of emission sources. |
| **18.3 Joint ventures and financial control consolidation approach** | GHG Accounting | When using a financial control consolidation approach, companies must disclose whether it has joint financial control of any of its joint ventures. Two scenarios may arise: 1. If the reporting company has joint financial control, they must include the emissions from that joint venture throughout scopes 1, 2, and 3 (categories 1-14), proportional to the equity held in that joint venture. 2. If the reporting company does not have joint financial control, they must include the scope 1 and 2 emissions of the joint venture in category 15, proportionate to the equity held in that joint venture. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: R335111, S615181; Completion of the "Company structure templat.csv" file with details of percentage ownership of the reporting company and all worldwide subsidiaries, joint ventures, equity holdings, and other entities, and upload of the completed file. |
| **18.4 Calculation methods** | GHG Accounting | Companies must use calculation methods consistent with the GHG Protocol Technical Guidance for Calculating Scope 3 emissions. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Questions: S61513; Provision of details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material. |

## ASSESSMENT OF SBTi CRITERIA FOR SECTOR-SPECIFIC TARGETS

---

### AVIATION SECTOR

*Table 4. Aviation Sector Criteria Assessment Table*

#### Aviation C1 — Applicability of Scope 1 and Scope 3 Category 3 Aviation SDA Targets

*The aviation sector guidance "SCIENCE-BASED TARGET SETTING FOR THE AVIATION SECTOR" and "Technical Report: The SBTi Interim 1.5°C Sector Pathway for Aviation" and associated aviation sector SDA targets are applicable to and optional for companies that derive 5% or more of their total scope 1 and 2 GHG emissions (tCO2e) from jet fuel combustion.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **1.1 Appropriate activities for aviation sector scope 1 and scope 3 category 3 SDA targets** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies must have jet fuel emissions within their organizational boundary, corresponding to scope 1 emissions that are 5% or more of total scope 1 and 2 emissions, in order to be eligible to set scope 1 and scope 3 category 3 aviation SDA targets aligned with or exceeding the 1.5°C pathway's minimum ambition. Cross-sector absolute reduction targets are also eligible over these emissions. The aviation SDA is currently only applicable to near-term targets. Sector agnostic long-term target setting methods must be used for net-zero submissions. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Overview; Questions: S52, S731; Provision of details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material. |
| **1.2 "SCIENCE-BASED TARGET SETTING FOR THE AVIATION SECTOR" supersedence** | Target Setting | Companies choosing to set aviation SDA targets following the target setting guidance in "SCIENCE-BASED TARGET SETTING FOR THE AVIATION SECTOR" for target formulation and calculation guidance must adhere to the latest target timeframe and ambition requirements at the time of submission. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV11.2.5, SAV11.2.5.1, SAV11.2.5.1.1, SAV11.2.10, SAV11.2.11, SAV11.2.13, SAV11.2.14, SAV11.2.19; Provision of the required information and selection of the ambition aligning with or exceeding the minimum ambition output for identical activity data. |
| **1.3 Long-Term Options** | Target Setting | Companies with validated 1.5°C aligned aviation SDA targets or that are setting new 1.5°C aligned aviation SDA targets in the near-term may set Net-Zero targets, in which case long-term targets must meet Net-Zero Criteria requirements for coverage and either cross-sector absolute reduction long-term target ambition or aviation SDA target ambition for the long-term target year. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Targets tab - Add long-term cross sector target - Absolute-cross sector or - Add long-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV11.2.5, SAV11.2.10, SAV11.2.19 for near-term SDA target; SAV11.4.5, SAV11.4.10, SAV11.4.19 for long-term SDA target; S11314, S11319 for long-term Absolute cross-sector target; Provision of the required information and selection of the ambition aligning with or exceeding the minimum ambition and target coverage requirements of the Net-Zero criteria and Aviation criteria respectively. |

---

#### Aviation C2 — Specific GHG Accounting Requirements

*Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets must adhere to the following aviation sector-specific considerations over sustainable aviation fuel (SAF) GHG accounting to align all aviation sector SDA inventory boundaries.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **2.1 Adherence to ICAO Sustainability Criteria** | Sector-Specific GHG Accounting | Companies intending to reflect SAF consumption in GHG emissions reporting in any reporting year related to science based targets must have certification for the consumed SAF against all ICAO sustainability criteria. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Fuel and energy related activities; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Upstream transportation and distribution; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Businesses travel; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Downstream transportation and distribution; Questions: S351, S3511, S3512, S3515, S3517, S52, S6313, S6326, S6413, S6613, S6913; Provision of supporting documentation such as the procured SAF's lifecycle data sheet corresponding to an ICAO approved verification and/or RSB certification where applicable. |
| **2.2 Adapt to GHG accounting updates** | GHG Accounting | Companies intending to reflect SAF consumption in GHG emissions reporting in any reporting year related to science based targets must follow the latest SAF emissions reporting requirement updates from the SBTi or those recognised by the SBTi. | Portal Location: Progress and Reporting; Questions: S1241, S1242, S1243, S1244, S1246, S1247, S1248; Confirmations of adherence to reporting criteria through all Questions indicated above. |
| **2.3 Appropriate emissions allocation** | GHG Accounting | Companies accounting for SAF consumption in their GHG inventory must ensure emissions allocation is in alignment with GHGP and existing SBTi precedent - the emissions from the combustion of the biogenic portion of the SAF and the LUC removals associated with the biogenic portion of the SAF must be accounted outside the scopes in biogenic emissions and removals reporting. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - General questions; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Fuel and energy related activities; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Upstream transportation and distribution; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Businesses travel; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Downstream transportation and distribution; Questions: S351, S3511, S3512, S3515, S3517, S52, S6313, S6326, S6413, S6613, S6913; Provision of biogenic emissions, removals, and details of calculation methods, assumptions, data sources and related material where applicable. |
| **2.4 SAF emissions and biogenic emissions footnote** | Target Setting | Any targets where SAF consumption and corresponding biogenic emissions exist in the base or most recent year, or are expected to arise in the target timeframe, must include the biogenic emissions footnote: "*The target boundary includes land-related emissions and removals from biogenic feedstocks." | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV11.2.23; Confirmation to include the footnote under the target wording. |

---

#### Aviation C3 — WTW Emissions Reporting and Target Boundaries

*Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets must cover Well-to-Wake (WTW) emissions related to jet fuel, covering the Well-to-Tank (WTT) emissions in category 3 and the Tank-to-Wake (TTW) emissions in scope 1, or WTW emissions related to jet fuel reported on a WTW basis in scope 3 categories 4, 6 or 9.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **3.1 WTW target boundary for companies with scope 1 jet fuel emissions** | Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets must cover WTW jet fuel emissions in target boundaries; for scope 1 jet fuel combustion emissions, companies must include the WTT emissions related to the jet fuel, reported in scope 3 category 3, in the target boundary. This supersedes SBTi Near-Term Criterion 4, 6 and 18, and applies irrespective of adherence to Near-Term Criterion 6. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Fuel and energy related activities; GHG Inventory tab - Overview; Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: S52, S6313, S731, SAV.11.2.5; Provision of breakdown of key scope 1 in Table 1 and scope 3 GHG emissions, alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes in the Aviation SDA target. |
| **3.2 WTW aviation SDA target boundary for upstream purchased aviation activities** | Target Setting | Companies choosing to set aviation sector SDA targets over upstream aviation activities (paid for by the reporting company) where corresponding emissions are reported in scope 3 category 4 must report such emissions in category 4 on a WTW basis and cover all WTW jet fuel emissions in the target boundary. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Upstream transportation and distribution; GHG Inventory tab - Overview; Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: S6413, S6423, S731, SAV.11.2.5; Confirmation and breakdown of key scope 3 GHG emissions, alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes in the Aviation SDA target. |
| **3.3 WTW target boundary for business travel aviation activities** | Target Setting | Companies choosing to set aviation sector targets over air business travel activities where corresponding emissions are reported in scope 3 category 6 must report such emissions in category 6 on a WTW basis and cover all WTW jet fuel emissions in the target boundary. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Businesses travel; GHG Inventory tab - Overview; Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: S6613, S6617, S731, SAV.11.2.5; Confirmation and breakdown of key scope 3 GHG emissions, alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes in the Aviation SDA target. |
| **3.4 WTW aviation SDA target boundary for downstream aviation activities** | Target Setting | Companies choosing to set aviation sector SDA targets over downstream aviation activities (not paid for by the reporting company) where corresponding emissions are reported in scope 3 category 9 must report such emissions in category 9 on a WTW basis and cover all WTW jet fuel emissions in the target boundary. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Downstream transportation and distribution; GHG Inventory tab - Overview; Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: S6913, S6923, S731, SAV.11.2.5; Confirmation and breakdown of key scope 3 GHG emissions, alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes in the Aviation SDA target. |

---

#### Aviation C4 — Suitable Baseline For Meaningful Targets

*Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets must ensure the selected base year is representative of current business activities and consistent across scope 1, 2 and 3.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **4.1 Representative baseline for meaningful target ambition** | Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets must ensure the base year chosen corresponds to emissions and activity volumes that are representative of the organizational boundary at the time of submission. Companies should avoid choosing base years where emissions magnitudes and revenue passenger kilometers (RPK) or revenue tonne kilometers (RTK) are significantly different from those in surrounding years, because of the significant impacts of activity levels on resulting target ambition. Consequently, companies setting aviation SDA targets must not use years from 2020 to 2022 as base years because of the substantial impact of the Covid-19 pandemic on activity resulting in anomalous emissions intensity. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Overview; Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: S741, SAV.11.2.14, SAV.11.2.19; Provision of supporting documents displaying recent trajectories in emissions, activities, output, revenue or other relevant metrics to justify the choice of base year. |

---

#### Aviation C5 — Disclosing Activity Projections To Set Ambitious Targets

*Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets must disclose and report base year, most recent year and target year activity data and credible and justifiable growth projections to determine minimum target ambition, which must be aligned with or exceed the 1.5°C pathway's minimum ambition for scope 1 and scope 3 category 3 targets and which must be aligned with or exceed the WB2C pathway's minimum ambition for solely scope 3 targets.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **5.1 Disclosure of current organization activity** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets over their own operations must disclose base year and most recent year revenue passenger kilometers (RPK) or revenue tonne kilometers (RTK) flown corresponding to scope 1 jet fuel emissions. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: Airline (including belly freight) - SAV.11.2.6, SAV.11.2.6.1, SAV.11.2.8, SAV.11.2.8.1; Dedicated freight - SAV.11.2.6.2, SAV.11.2.8.2; Provision of activity data for base year and most recent year. |
| **5.2 Disclosure of credible and justifiable organization activity projections** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets over their own operations must disclose credible and justifiable projected target year revenue passenger kilometers (RPK) or revenue tonne kilometers (RTK) flown corresponding to scope 1 jet fuel emissions, either in the form of a consistent compound annual growth rate (CAGR) or a target year activity. It is recommended that companies use company-specific data for the activity projections, but, if necessary, companies may consider other credible sources with robust justification and evidence for the activity projection representativeness. | Questions: SAV.11.2.13, SAV.11.2.14; Provision of supporting documents displaying that business planning and recent trajectories in activities, output, revenue or other relevant metrics result in the growth projections included for setting the target. |
| **5.3 Disclosure of current upstream aviation sector activity** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets over WTW jet fuel emissions emissions reported in scope 3 category 4: upstream transportation and distribution, corresponding to purchased and sub-contracted flights, must disclose corresponding base year and most recent year revenue passenger kilometers (RPK) or revenue tonne kilometers (RTK) flown. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: Airline (including belly freight) - SAV.11.2.6, SAV.11.2.6.1, SAV.11.2.8, SAV.11.2.8.1; Dedicated freight - SAV.11.2.6.2, SAV.11.2.8.2; Provision of activity data for base year and most recent year. |
| **5.4 Disclosure of current downstream aviation sector activity** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets over WTW jet fuel emissions emissions reported in scope 3 category 9: downstream transportation and distribution, corresponding to aviation activities they have not paid for, must disclose corresponding base year and most recent year revenue passenger kilometers (RPK) or revenue tonne kilometers (RTK) flown. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: Airline (including belly freight) - SAV.11.2.6, SAV.11.2.6.1, SAV.11.2.8, SAV.11.2.8.1; Dedicated freight - SAV.11.2.6.2, SAV.11.2.8.2; Provision of activity data for base year and most recent year. |
| **5.5 Disclosure of credible and justifiable upstream activity projections** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets over WTW jet fuel emissions reported in scope 3 category 4: upstream transportation and distribution, corresponding to purchased and sub-contracted flights, must disclose credible and justifiable corresponding projected target year revenue passenger kilometers (RPK) or revenue tonne kilometers (RTK) flown, either in the form of a consistent compound annual growth rate (CAGR) or a target year activity. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV.11.2.11, SAV.11.2.12, SAV.11.2.13, SAV.11.2.14; Provision of supporting documents displaying that business planning and recent trajectories in activities, output, revenue or other relevant metrics result in the growth projections included for setting the target. |
| **5.6 Disclosure of credible and justifiable downstream activity projections** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets over WTW jet fuel emissions reported in scope 3 category 9: downstream transportation and distribution, corresponding to aviation activities they have not paid for, must disclose credible and justifiable corresponding projected target year revenue passenger kilometers (RPK) or revenue tonne kilometers (RTK) flown downstream. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV.11.2.11, SAV.11.2.12, SAV.11.2.13, SAV.11.2.14; Provision of supporting documents displaying that business planning and recent trajectories in activities, output, revenue or other relevant metrics result in the growth projections included for setting the target. |
| **5.7 Owned aviation operations minimum ambition requirements** | Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets over their own aviation operations (covering scope 1 and scope 3 category 3 jet fuel emissions) must align with or exceed the minimum ambition of the convergence curve corresponding to the 1.5°C aviation sector pathway and their unique emissions and activity, as output by the "aviation target setting tool 2.0". | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV.11.2.5, SAV.11.2.19; Provision of the required information and selection of the ambition aligning with or exceeding the minimum ambition output. |
| **5.8 Value chain aviation operations minimum ambition requirements** | Target Setting | Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets over value chain aviation operations (either covering scope 3 category 4 or category 9 WTW jet fuel emissions) must align with or exceed the minimum ambition of the convergence curve corresponding to the WB2C aviation sector pathway and their unique emissions and activity, as output by the "aviation target setting tool 2.0". | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV.11.2.5, SAV.11.2.19; Provision of the required information and selection of the ambition aligning with or exceeding the minimum ambition output. |
| **5.9 Business travel aviation target method and ambition exception** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies choosing to set aviation sector targets over business air travel emissions, which may be displayed as intensity reductions per full time employee equivalent, must ensure ambition equals or exceeds the minimum linear annual reduction of the cross-sector absolute reduction WB2C pathway. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV.11.2.2, SAV.11.2.5, SAV.11.2.6.3, SAV.11.2.7.3, SAV.11.2.10, SAV.11.2.11.5; Provision of activity data for base year, most recent year and target year. |
| **5.10 Minimum ambition adjustments for target updates** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies with existing aviation SDA targets and updating to new SDA targets must ensure the new target ambition corresponds to lower target year emissions where the target year remains consistent. Companies must ensure the target ambition corresponds to lower emissions targeted along the convergence curve than the previously validated SDA target's convergence curve in cases where the target year is not consistent. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV11.2.5, SAV11.2.19; Provision of the required information and selection of the ambition aligning with or exceeding the minimum ambition output. |

---

#### Aviation C6 — Aviation Specific Public Reporting Requirements

*Companies setting aviation sector SDA targets should publicly report target related information with the utmost transparency. Companies must publicly report on progress against targets and associated commitments.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **6.1 Commitment to report through the non-GHG impacts footnote** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies setting aviation SDA targets must commit, through a footnote to their targets, to reporting on non-GHG potential warming impacts and their efforts to determine and avoid non-GHG warming impacts of aviation either directly or through collaboration with others in the field. The footnote must be either: A) "*Non-CO₂ factors which may also contribute to aviation induced warming are not included in this target. [Company Name] [currently publicly reports/will publicly report] its non-CO2 impacts." OR B) "*Non-CO2e effects which may also contribute to aviation induced warming are not included in this target. [Company Name] commits to report publicly on its collaboration with stakeholders to improve understanding of the opportunities to mitigate the non-CO2e impacts of aviation annually over its target timeframe." | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Aviation SDA; Questions: SAV11.2.22; Confirmation to include the footnote under the target wording. |

### BUILDINGS SECTOR

*Table 5. Buildings Sector Criteria Assessment Table*

#### Buildings C1 — Thresholds for In-Use Operational Emissions

*Companies whose business activities meet any of the intended user categories in Buildings-C3 and whose in-use operational emissions from owned and/or managed buildings are at least 20% of their total scope 1, 2, and 3 category 1-14 emissions in their chosen base year shall apply these criteria in full and set a target on in-use operational emissions.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **1.1 In-use Operational Emissions Calculations** | GHG Accounting | For each applicable user type, companies must calculate and allocate GHG emissions in accordance with the whole building approach. The whole building approach requires companies to include emissions arising from operational energy consumption of all landlord and tenant controlled spaces in their GHG inventory, regardless of the chosen consolidation approach (refer to C6 below). The reported inventory shall also include fugitive emissions for both tenant and landlord controlled areas. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Use of sold products; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Downstream leased assets; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Overview; Questions: S52, S522, S61113, S61313, S731; Confirmation and description of key scope 1 and 2 business activities and breakdown of key scope 1 and 2 emissions, scope 3 category 11 (Use of sold products) and/or scope 3 category 13 (Downstream leased assets) GHG emissions. |
| **1.2 Total GHG Inventory Emissions Calculations** | GHG Accounting | After allocating emissions per user type in line with the whole building approach, companies must determine the percentage of total scope 1, 2, and 3 in-use emissions that come from owned, operated, and/or managed buildings. Companies must also consider the exclusions from the GHG inventory in determining the total scope 1, 2, and 3 in-use emissions and in determining whether the threshold detailed in C1.3 below is met. The exclusions from the buildings related in-use operational emissions in the base year shall be considered within and part of the total allowable exclusions across the scopes accordingly as stated in near-term criterion NT C5. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Upstream leased assets; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Use of sold products; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Downstream leased assets; Questions: S52, S522, S6813, S61113, S61313; Confirmation and justification of any exclusions from the scope 1, 2 and relevant scope 3 GHG emissions in tCO2e. Total excluded emissions for scope 1, 2 and scope 3 category 1-14 must be entered in Question 2.2 of the Buildings Annex. |
| **1.3 Mandatory in-use operational emissions target** | Sector-Specific Target Setting | Companies whose business activities meet the intended user categories as mentioned in Buildings C3 below and whose corresponding in-use operational emissions from owned, operated and/or managed buildings are at least 20% of their total scope 1, 2, and 3 category 1-14 emissions in their chosen base year must set a Buildings In-Use Operational Emissions SDA target. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Overview; Targets tab - Add near-term sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Questions: S731, S11220 (near-term), S11420 (long-term); Companies must submit targets to the SBTi that are modeled using the official SBTi Buildings target setting tool published on the SBTi website. The tool must be uploaded in the validation portal for relevant targets in the format of an excel file. |

---

#### Buildings C2 — Thresholds for Upfront Embodied Emissions of New Constructed Buildings

*Companies whose business activities meet any of the intended user categories in Buildings-C3 and whose upfront embodied emissions from new developments or acquisitions of a building as a first owner exceeded 20% of total scope 1, 2, and 3 category 1-14 emissions in any one year within the previous three years shall apply the criteria in full and set a target on upfront embodied emissions.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **2.1 Applicability for developers** | Sector-Specific | Companies that fall under the definition and business activities of the developer as defined in Table 5 of SBTi Buildings Explanatory document that choose to account for upfront embodied emissions of the buildings at practical completion treating the buildings as a 'capital good' or on an annual basis within scope 3 category 1 shall adhere to the threshold requirements outlined in Buildings-C2. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Capital goods; Questions: S6213, S626; Confirmation and description of key business activities and corresponding emissions in the GHG inventory section of the validation portal and Questions 2.1 and 2.5 of the Buildings Annex. |
| **2.2 Defining the first owner of a building** | Sector-Specific | Companies that meet any of the intended user categories as stated in Buildings-C3 that have acquired or purchased new buildings either through sale or transfer of ownership by the developer shall be considered a first owner when they start the use phase of a new building. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Capital goods; Questions: S6213, S626; Confirmation and description of key business activities and corresponding emissions in the GHG inventory section of the validation portal and Questions 2.1 and 2.4 of the Buildings Annex. |
| **2.3 GHG Inventory Emissions Calculations** | Sector-Specific | Companies classified as first owners shall report upstream emissions from the extraction, production, and transportation of building materials, including all emissions related to the construction of the building in scope 3 category 2 capital goods. This aligns with the LCA modules A1 to A5 that cover the production and construction phases of a building's life cycle which are referred to as 'upfront carbon' as per the EN 15978 standard. Companies must also consider the exclusions from the GHG inventory in determining the total scope 1, 2, and 3 upfront embodied emissions and in determining whether the threshold detailed in C2.4 below is met. The exclusions from the buildings related upfront embodied emissions accounted for in scope 3 category 2 capital goods shall be considered within and part of the total allowable exclusions across total scope 3 emissions as stated in the near-term criterion NT C5. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3; Question: S61; Confirmation and breakdown of key scope 3 GHG emissions scope 1, 2, 3 categories 1-14 and Question 2.7 of the Buildings Annex. |
| **2.4 Mandatory upfront embodied emissions target** | Sector-Specific | Companies that meet any of the intended user categories in Buildings-C3 and whose upfront embodied emissions from new developments or acquisitions of a building as a first owner exceeded 20% of total scope 1, 2, and 3 (categories 1-14) emissions in any one year within the three years prior to the year of target submission shall apply the criteria in full and set a target on upfront embodied emissions, in line with the timeframe specified in Buildings-C9, using the buildings target setting tool. | Companies must submit targets to the SBTi that are modeled using the official SBTi target setting tools published on the SBTi website. The tool must be uploaded in the validation portal for relevant targets in the format of an excel file. |

---

#### Buildings C3 — Intended User Categorization

*Companies shall apply the relevant target-setting criteria for all intended user types that are applicable to their business activities. Companies must also briefly explain their choice of intended user categorization when submitting targets for validation. These criteria and recommendations address the following user categories, whilst acknowledging that classifications might differ between markets and jurisdictions internationally: Developer; Owner-occupier; Owner-lessor; Property manager; Financial institution (FI)\*. \*It is important to note that a company, categorized primarily as a non-FI intended user may undertake activities (i.e. investments) that fall under the FI category. For example, an integrated real estate company.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **3.1 Intended user categorization** | Sector-Specific | Companies must disclose and justify their selection of applicability for each intended user categorization(s) listed in Buildings C3 (i.e., developer, owner-occupier, owner-lessor, and property manager). | Written explanation in Question 2.1 of the Buildings Annex. |
| **3.2 Relevant target setting guidance application** | Target Setting | Companies must apply the relevant target-setting guidance for all intended user types (i.e., developer, owner-occupier, owner-lessor and property manager) that are applicable to their business activities. Companies shall refer to Buildings C1 and Buildings C2 for assessing target setting applicability and Buildings C4 for all applicable target setting methods. | Confirmation in Question 2.1 and Sections 4 and 5 of the Buildings Annex alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes in the SBTi Buildings target setting tool. |

---

#### Buildings C4 — Permitted Target-Setting Methods

*Permitted target-setting methods for scope 1, 2 and 3 buildings-related emissions for buildings sector users are laid out in Tables 1a-1d of the SBTi Buildings Criteria document. Owner-occupiers and owner-lessors shall use the buildings in-use operational emissions SDA to set a target on their whole building in-use operational emissions, irrespective of whether these emissions are categorized as scope 1, 2, or 3 emissions.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **4.1 Buildings targets 1.5°C minimum ambition** | Sector-Specific | Companies setting buildings SDA or sector-specific absolute contraction targets must ensure target ambition equals or exceeds the minimum 1.5°C ambition alignment output by the Buildings target setting tool, regardless of the scope and category in which the covered emissions are allocated in the GHG inventory. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Overview; Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings Upfront embodied target; Questions: S731; S11219 (near-term), S11419 (long-term) for Buildings in-use operational; SBU.11.2.19 (near-term), SBU.11.4.19 (long-term) for Buildings upfront embodied target; Confirmation of target language and ambition in Section 5 of the Buildings Annex. Corresponding emissions boundaries must be entered in the SBTi buildings target setting tool (the aggregator tab must be used when the company owns and/or operates multiple buildings to demonstrate that the target ambition selected equals or exceeds the requirement.) |
| **4.2 Mandatory in-use operational emissions targets** | Target Setting | Companies that satisfy Buildings C1 thresholds with in-use operational buildings emissions must set the in-use operational SDA target as shown in Table 1a of the SBTi Buildings Criteria document. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Use of sold products; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Downstream leased assets; Questions: S52, S522, S61113, S61313; Confirmation and description of key scope 1 and 2 business activities and breakdown of key scope 1 and 2 emissions and scope 3 category 13 (Downstream leased assets) GHG emissions. Additional breakdowns must be provided in Question 2.1 and 2.2 of the Buildings Annex. |
| **4.3 Localized in-use operational emissions targets** | Target Setting | Companies setting in-use operational buildings SDA targets must disaggregate total portfolio emissions and floor area by geography and building typology in order to determine the geography and building typology specific reduction requirements that shall be aggregated into the overall in-use operational emissions target by utilizing the aggregator tab in the Buildings target setting tool. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Questions: S1122, S1123 for near-term targets; S1142, S1143 for long-term targets; Confirmation and description in Questions 2.1, 2.2, 3.1, 3.2, 3.3, and 3.4 with a breakdown of scope 1, 2 and 3 emissions per user type, building type, region, country and sub-region/state in Table 1 of the Buildings Annex. Provision of corresponding emissions magnitudes in the aggregator SBTi Buildings target setting tool which is uploaded for the relevant target in the Validation Portal. |
| **4.4 Fixed intensity targets over in-use operational emissions** | Sector Specific | Companies and financial institutions with high turnover portfolios that are classified as an owner-occupier, owner-lessor, and/or a financial institution must demonstrate high portfolio turnover is integral to their business model if they are to set fixed intensity targets over in-use operational emissions. This may be met by the following examples: (1) The user is an opportunistic fund that acquires older and less efficient buildings and renovates the buildings prior to sale. The company may have no common assets over a 36-month period. (2) The user is an 'instant buyer' such as a real estate company that uses algorithms and technology to buy and resell residential buildings in quick succession. (3) The user has a historical and/or projected average buildings portfolio turnover ratio over the next 5-10 years of over 70%, where the yearly ratio is defined as: Portfolio turnover ratio (%) = (|Divested building floor area (m²)| + |Acquired building floor area (m²)|) / Average portfolio area (m²) × 100. Companies and financial institutions choosing to use fixed intensity targets shall demonstrate why/how their portfolio turnover makes target-setting with the SDA not applicable using the examples provided in the explanatory document. Please note that significant growth projections are not a sufficient justification for high turnover, as growth is factored into SDA target calculations. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Questions: S11213, S11214, S1125, S11219, S11220; Provision of supporting documents displaying that business planning and recent trajectories in activities, output, revenue or other relevant metrics result in the growth projections included in the target setting tool. Confirmation in Questions 4.9, 4.10 and Table 1 of the Buildings Annex alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes in the SBTi Buildings target setting tool which is uploaded in the Validation Portal. |
| **4.5 Applicability of the maintenance targets over in-use operational emissions** | Sector Specific | Companies and financial institutions classified as an owner-lessor, owner-occupier and/or FI that meet the following condition may set a maintenance target covering in-use operational emissions: Corporates and financial institutions must have a portfolio emissions intensity that is at or below the 2050 sector intensity level of a 1.5°C-aligned pathway for its building typology and geography-specific pathway in the base year. Corporates and financial institutions must also commit to maintain the base year portfolio emissions intensity through the near-term and long-term target timeframes and only finance and/or own and/or lease 1.5°C aligned real estate assets. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Questions: S1125, S1126, S11214, S11219, S11220; Provision of in-use emissions, floor area and carbon intensity (kgCO₂e/m²) for each building type and location in the aggregator tab of the SBTi buildings target setting tool to demonstrate that weighted average emissions intensity levels are at or below the 2050 weighted intensity or at or below the lowest 2050 intensity of the relevant pathways. Written explanation in Questions 4.11 and 4.12 of the Buildings Annex detailing how the applicability is met. |
| **4.6 Disclosure of credible and justifiable in-use floor area projections** | Sector-Specific | Companies setting in-use operational SDA targets must provide credible and justifiable projections for target year floor area for each relevant geography and building typology selected in the Buildings target setting tool when providing target year projections. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Questions: S11211, S112111, S11213, S11214, S11220; Confirmation and provision of supporting documents displaying that business planning and recent trajectories in activities, output, revenue or other relevant metrics result in the growth projections included in the target setting tool uploaded in the Validation Portal for the relevant target. |
| **4.7 Upfront embodied emissions SDA targets** | Target Setting | Companies setting upfront embodied buildings SDA targets must disaggregate total emissions and floor area by the specific building type (residential, office, retail or other) in order to determine the aggregated emissions reduction ambition. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Upfront embodied emissions target; Questions: SBU.11.2.5, SBU.11.2.6, SBU.11.2.14, SBU.11.2.19, SBU.11.2.20 for near-term target; SBU.11.4.5, SBU.11.4.6, SBU.11.4.14, SBU.11.4.19, SBU.11.4.20 for long-term target; Confirmation in Questions 4.5 and 4.6, and breakdown of emissions in Table 1 of the Buildings Annex alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes in the SBTi Buildings target setting tool. The emissions magnitudes in the Buildings target setting tool must match the targets reported in Questions 5.4 and 5.5 of the Buildings Annex and those covered under the target as reported in the Validation Portal. |
| **4.8 Disclosure of credible and justifiable developed floor area projections** | Sector-Specific | Companies setting upfront embodied SDA targets must provide credible and justifiable projections of target year floor area for each specific building type selected in the Buildings target setting tool when providing target year projections. | Portal Location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Upfront embodied emissions target; Questions: SBU.11.2.11, SBU.11.2.13, SBU.11.2.14, SBU.11.2.20 for the near-term target; SBU.11.4.11, SBU.11.4.13, SBU.11.4.14, SBU.11.4.20 for long-term target; Provision of supporting documents displaying that business planning and recent trajectories in activities, output, revenue or other relevant metrics result in the growth projections included in the target setting tool uploaded in the validation for the relevant target. |

| **4.9 Lifetime in-use operational emissions targets** | Target Setting | Companies setting targets over lifetime in-use operational emissions of sold buildings must select an ambition level that equals or exceeds the minimum ambition output generated by the latest version of the "Science-Based Target Setting Tool" at the time of submission, setting either a 1.5°C absolute reduction target, an economic intensity target or a physical intensity target. | Targets tab - Add near term target; Questions: S1114, S11119; Confirmation and breakdown of key scope 3 GHG emissions scope 3 categories 11 emissions. Corresponding emissions boundaries and outputs entered to demonstrate that the target ambition selected equals or exceeds the requirement. |
| **4.10 Buildings targets recalculation and target validity** | Sector Specific | All companies setting emissions reduction targets through the SBTi are subject to SBTi general criteria, which requires validated targets be reviewed, and if necessary, updated and revalidated, at a minimum every 5 years from the date of the target approval. Additionally, existing targets shall be recalculated and/or revalidated, as needed, to reflect significant changes that compromise the existing target. Please refer to NT C26, NT C27, NZ C32 and NZ C33 for further context. In the buildings sector the following changes shall be treated as significant changes, each of which triggers a target recalculation for SDA targets set under the Buildings Criteria using the Buildings target setting tool: (1) Significant changes in the building typology and/or geographical composition of portfolios; (2) New geographies and/or building typologies are added to the portfolio (e.g. through acquisition, development, or business expansion); (3) A significant proportion of the total portfolio floor area, as stated in the base year, has changed the building typology due to major renovations; (4) Acquisition or development of new buildings leading to a potential change in whether the condition outlined in Buildings-C2 is met. This may result in the user being defined as a first owner and being eligible to set an upfront embodied emissions target. The 10% threshold used for defining significant changes is based on whether a building within existing geographies and building types enters or exits the portfolio or if a building outside existing geographies and building types enters the portfolio of the SDA target. This is explained further in Section 6.4.2 of the Buildings Sector Science-Based Targets Explanatory Document. | Agreement to recalculate targets in Question 6.2 of the Buildings Annex if any SBTi sector specific significant changes for the Buildings SDA targets that compromise the relevance and consistency of existing targets. |

---

#### Buildings C5 — Choosing Pathways

*When using the buildings SDAs, users shall select the most appropriate building typology and geographic location for their buildings and shall adhere to the SBTi Buildings Target-Setting Tool in choosing an appropriate pathway (selecting building typologies and geographies), including available guidance for when a named pathway is not available. Buildings that are not covered by the building typologies and/or geographies provided in the latest version of the tool shall use the 'Other' pathway.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **5.1 Most appropriate pathway adoption** | Target Setting | Companies setting buildings SDA targets must select the most appropriate building typology pathway for their region/geographic location in the latest version of the tool at the time of submission, adopting the 'Other' pathway when a named pathway is not available for a specific region/geographic location. | Portal location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings Upfront embodied emissions target; Questions: S1122, S1123, S11220 for Buildings in-use operational targets; SBU.11.2.2, SBU.11.2.20 for Buildings upfront embodied emissions SDA target; Within Table 1 of the Buildings Annex, companies must provide GHG emissions data with a breakdown of scope 1, 2 and 3 emissions per user type, building type, region, country and sub-region/state. Companies must submit targets to the SBTi that are modeled using the official SBTi Buildings target setting tool published on the SBTi website. Any tool used must be uploaded in the format of an excel file and included in the reporting company's submission files. |
| **5.2 Mixed-use buildings** | Target Setting | For mixed-use buildings, companies shall use the appropriate floor area and emissions associated with a relevant building typology and set different targets over each relevant building typology. When doing so, companies must ensure the proportional floor areas of the different building typologies sums up to the total floor area of the mixed-use building. For mixed-use assets reporting for in-use operational emissions where one typology represents at least 90% of the floor area, companies may select the typology which represents the highest share of floor area of the building (e.g., a building with 92% residential and 8% retail space could be categorized as 100% residential). For mixed-use assets for upfront embodied emissions, companies should select the typology which represents the highest share of floor area of the building (e.g., a building with 40% residential and 60% retail space would be categorized as 100% 'retail'). | Portal location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings Upfront embodied emissions target; Questions: S1122, S1123, S11220 for Buildings in-use operational targets; SBU.11.2.2, SBU.11.2.20 for Buildings upfront embodied emissions SDA target; Confirmation to Questions 4.2.1 and 4.2.2 in the Buildings Annex and provision of corresponding emissions magnitudes in the SBTi Buildings target setting tool uploaded in the Validation Portal for relevant targets. |

---

#### Buildings C6 — Whole Building Approach

*Companies shall include all emissions arising from operational energy consumption from both landlord and tenant-controlled spaces within target boundaries, regardless of their chosen GHG boundary consolidation approach and consequent allocation of emissions across their inventory. Property managers shall adhere to the whole building approach if they set an SDA target for in-use operational emissions.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **6.1 Whole building GHG accounting** | GHG Accounting | Companies satisfying Buildings C1, and companies whose business activities meet the intended user categories developer, owner-occupier and owner lessor, must adopt the 'whole building approach', meaning that the inclusion of emissions arising from operational energy consumption from all landlord and tenant controlled spaces is required in their GHG inventory, regardless of the company's chosen consolidation approach. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Downstream leased assets; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Overview; Questions: S52, S522, S61313, S731; Confirmation and description of key scope 1 and 2 business activities and breakdown of key scope 1 and 2 emissions and scope 3 category 13 (Downstream leased assets) GHG emissions. Additional breakdown of emissions in Table 1 of the Buildings Annex alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes in the SBTi buildings target setting tool uploaded in the Validation Portal for relevant targets. |
| **6.2 Whole building GHG accounting for property managers** | GHG Accounting | Companies satisfying Buildings C1, and companies whose business activities meet the intended user category property manager that are setting an in-use operational emissions Buildings SDA target must also adopt the 'whole building approach.' As mentioned in C6.1, this refers to the inclusion of emissions arising from operational energy consumption in all landlord and tenant controlled spaces within a company's GHG inventory, regardless of the company's chosen consolidation approach. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Use of sold products or GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Downstream leased assets; Questions: S61113, S6115, S61313; Confirmation and description of key business activities and breakdown of GHG emissions. Confirmation to Question 2.1 with an additional breakdown of emissions in Table 1 of the Buildings Annex. Corresponding emissions magnitudes must be entered in the SBTi Buildings target setting tool uploaded in the Validation Portal for relevant targets. |

---

#### Buildings C7 — Fugitive Emissions

*Companies must include fugitive emissions, from all building types, within their in-use operational emissions and as part of both their GHG inventory and target boundaries.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **7.1 Inclusion of fugitive emissions** | GHG Accounting | Companies must include fugitive emissions from all building types within their in-use operational GHG emissions calculations and consequently as part of both their GHG inventory and target boundaries. This includes fugitive emissions within direct control in scope 1, as well as fugitive emissions linked to leased and/or managed properties in scope 3 if relevant. | Portal Location: GHG Inventory tab - Scope 1; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 2; GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Use of sold products (optional for property managers, please refer to Buildings C6); GHG Inventory tab - Scope 3 - Downstream leased assets; Questions: S52, S522, S61113, S61313; Confirmation and description of key business activities and breakdown of GHG emissions and respond to Question 3.1 of the Buildings Annex. |

---

#### Buildings C8 — Required Scope 3 Categories

*All companies are required to report emissions that are applicable to their user type. For each user type and scope 3 category, these emissions may either be covered in the target boundary of a company's buildings SDA target when the corresponding thresholds for Buildings-C1 or Buildings-C2 are triggered, or in the boundary of a company's cross-sector target where applicable. Companies that trigger Buildings-C1 and/or Buildings-C2 and have less than 40% of their total emissions in scope 3 must cover all required emissions from the user-types included in the threshold determination within their target boundary. Coverage requirements of emissions outside of these applicable buildings-related emissions sources shall follow the cross-sector or eligible sector-specific criteria. All emissions categories required per user type are outlined in Table 2. These emissions must be included in either the target boundary of a company's buildings SDA targets if required, or in their cross-sector target when applicable.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **8.1 Complete target coverage of relevant buildings-related emissions** | Target Setting | Companies satisfying Buildings C1 and/or C2 must cover the buildings-related emissions under the required scope 3 targets as detailed in Table 2 of SBTi Buildings Criteria document. If a company has less than 40% of its emissions in scope 3 taking into account exclusions, all scope 3 emissions that fall under required target setting approaches as per Buildings C1, Buildings C2 and Buildings C3 must be covered by these targets. | Portal location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings Upfront embodied emissions target; Questions: S1125 (near-term), SBI1145 (long-term) for Buildings in-use operational; SBU.11.2.5, SBU.11.4.5 for Buildings upfront embodied target; Confirmation and breakdown of key scope 3 GHG emissions. Completion of section 2.3, 3.4, and Table 1 of the Buildings Annex alongside corresponding emissions magnitudes in the SBTi Buildings target setting tool uploaded in the Validation Portal for relevant targets. |
| **8.2 Scope 3 cross-sector targets** | Target Setting | Coverage requirements of emissions outside of these applicable buildings-related emissions sources shall follow the cross-sector or eligible sector-specific criteria. Companies with over 40% of total GHG emissions in scope 3 must set additional scope 3 targets using cross sector methods when the 67% scope 3 coverage requirement is not met by the buildings SDA targets alone in accordance with the SBTi's general criteria. The Buildings SDA targets set in line with Tables 1a-1d of the Buildings Criteria and other cross-sector targets must on aggregate meet the 67% minimum scope 3 coverage threshold even when taking into account exclusions. | Submission of the SBTi target setting tool and conformance with the target coverage formula in Table 8 and Table 10 of the submission form. |

---

#### Buildings C9 — Base Year for Upfront Embodied Emissions

*The base year for upfront embodied emissions targets must be no earlier than three years prior to the year of submission of the targets.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **9.1 Sufficiently recent base year** | Target Setting | Companies setting upfront embodied emissions targets must choose a base year that is no earlier than 3 years prior to the year of submission. | Confirmation to Question 2.5 and enter relevant GHG emissions data in Question 2.6 of the Buildings Annex. |
| **9.2 Representative base year** | Target Setting | Companies setting upfront embodied emissions targets must ensure that the chosen base year corresponds to emissions and activity volumes that are representative of the organizational boundary at the time of submission. Companies shall avoid choosing base years where emissions magnitudes and floor area developed are significantly different from those in surrounding years to ensure targets are meaningful, ambitious and achievable. | Portal location: GHG inventory tab - Scope 3 - Capital goods; GHG inventory tab - Scope 3 - Overview; Questions: S625, S741; Provision of supporting documents displaying recent trajectories in emissions, activities, output, revenue or other relevant metrics to justify the choice of base year. |

---

#### Buildings C10 — Denominator for Intensity-Based Targets

*The intensity pathway for the buildings SDAs must be expressed in terms of tCO₂e/m². For the calculation of intensities, which require a consistent floor area definition as a denominator, the floor area definition used must be applied consistently to a company's GHG accounting and across base and target years. In determining floor area, common areas (e.g. corridors, public lobbies etc.) must be included in accordance with the whole building approach.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **10.1 Suitable intensity metric format** | Sector-Specific | Companies setting buildings intensity-based targets must express the emissions intensity in terms of tCO2e/m². | Portal location: Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings in-use operational; Targets tab - Add sector specific target - Buildings Upfront embodied emissions target; Questions: S1124, S1126, S1128 for Buildings in-use operational near-term target; SBI1146, SBI1148 for Buildings in-use operational long-term target; SBU.11.2.4, SBU.11.2.6, SBU.11.2.8 for Buildings Upfront embodied emissions SDA near-term target; SBU.11.4.4, SBU.11.4.6, SBU.11.4.8 for Buildings Upfront embodied emissions SDA long-term target; Upload SBTi Buildings target setting tool with appropriate activity metrics and completion of the Buildings Annex form that is specific to the SBTi Buildings Criteria information. |
| **10.2 Consistent floor area determination** | Sector-Specific | Companies must include all common areas in accordance with the 'whole building approach' in determination of the floor area for use in target setting. Alignment with international standards such as the International Property Measurement Standard is strongly recommended. | Confirmation of adherence to criteria through submissions targets using Validation Portal and inclusion of all relevant areas in the uploaded Buildings Annex. |

---

#### Buildings C11 — Building Lifetime Assumptions in Use of Sold Products

*Users accounting for scope 3 category 11 use of sold products must disclose the building lifetime assumptions used. If a company chooses to use another lifetime estimate than what is recommended in Buildings R5 of the SBTi Buildings Criteria document, the lifetime assumptions they are using must be explained.*

| CAI | Applicability | Description | Minimum Documentation Required |
|-----|--------------|-------------|-------------------------------|
| **11.1 Lifetime in-use operational emissions in use of sold products** | GHG Accounting | Companies selling new buildings to the first owner must account for the lifetime in-use operational emissions associated with the sold asset.
